 summary : <p>About the ToolkitThe Force.com Toolkit for Google Data APIs provides a free and open-source set of tools and services that developers can use to take advantage of Google Data APIs from within Force.com.  </p>

<p>The goal of the toolkit is to make Google Data APIs – starting with Spreadsheets, Documents and Calendar – easy to use from within the Force.com environment.  </p>

<p>The toolkit is modeled after the Java Client library for Google Data, with many of the same class and method names.  In some cases the names have been changed to fit with Apex Code naming conventions. </p>

<p>The Classes found here expose the Google APIs directly within Apex, making it easier to access them natively from Force.com apps and providing tighter integration between the platforms with less developer effort. </p>

<p>For a user not familiar with the Force.com platform, this cloud development platform provides a robust and trusted application development and delivery environment for businesses large and small. </p>

<p>Apex ProgramersFor programmers of Apex Code, there is a wealth of reusable code and great examples of writing Test Methods to achieve high code coverage. </p>

<p>Of particular interest is the XmlDom and XmlDom Element classes, these are reusable in any a number of API integrations, this class has been tested with Google REST, Amazon, RSS and  Ebay API&#39;s to mention a few.  It will parse incoming XML and turn it into an Apex object (DOM) that can be accessed by standard methods like getElementByTagName() and firstChild(), each element contains a nodeValue, sound familiar? </p>

<p>This and much more can be found in the source tree here, drop a note if you would like to contribute! </p>

<p>Share and Enjoy. </p>

<p>Force.com project team</p>

<p>::Sobre o Projeto::Reunião inicial 20/08/2008 </p>

<p>A Vertigo Computação foi criada em 1999 e tem foco em sistemas de missão crítica, integração de legados, arquitetura SOA, mapeamento de processos de negócio BPM. Amplo domínio das plataformas JEE5 e BEA. </p>

<p>Em 2005 a Vertigo tinha de 5 a 7 colaboradores. Hoje já são aproximadamente 50 e com expectativa de crescer ainda mais. </p>

<p>Um dos processos que a Vertigo pretende controlar é o de controle de custos e métricas de projetos. O que a Vertigo realmente necessita é de um:  </p>

<p>Sistema de Controle dos Gastos Indiretos em Projetos </p>

<p>Processos que supostamente serão informatizados: </p>

<p>- A princípio, tudo que está relacionado a gastos indiretos dos projetos. </p>

<p>- Solicitação de diárias </p>

<p>- Aprovação de diárias </p>

<p>- Controle do pagamento de diárias </p>

<p>- Solicitação de Vourchers </p>

<p>- Relatórios diversos </p>

<p>Todo gasto está relacionado a um cliente e um projeto. Esses dados servem de base para a Vertigo receber seus honorários. </p>

<p>Na Vertigo, como em muitas empresas de informática, seus funcionários são convidados a permanecerem na empresa até mais tarde. Ex.: Até Às 23:55, sábados, etc. </p>

<p>Restrições: </p>

<p>- Todas as reuniões deverão ser marcadas após  18:00 para facilitar  o acesso aos  interessados. </p>

<p>- A aplicação deverá utilizar banco de dados MYSQL porque eles já possuem softwares internos neste banco de dados. </p>

<p>- Servidor de aplicação poderá ser WEBLOGIC da BEA(a confirmar). </p>

<p>- Plataforma JEE5 </p>

<p>- O sistema vai ter que funcionar perfeitamente para o negócio mesmo que seja necessário cortar escopo ou separar em releases. </p>

<p>- No ambiente de produção, a aplicação deverá rodar em servidor linux com conteiner a ser definido. </p>

<p>Premissas: </p>

<p>- Todos os integrantes poderão ter acesso a Vertigo. </p>

<p>Requisitos não funcionais: </p>

<p>- O sistema deverá suportar navegadores Internet Explorer e Firefox para estações Windows e Firefox para estações Linux. </p>

 summary : <p>Current StatusThis project is no longer the main project of the original developers, we are changing our focus to new software for the official SDK release.  This does not mean we are stopping working, this just means that it isn&#39;t our primary focus.  The full source + lib purple is in the SVN under apollo_1.02.  Since we can&#39;t work on it as much as we&#39;d like, we encourage anyone and everyone to get the source and start working on it.  If you want to see your changes merged back into the main source tree, send it to humajime @ gmail.com.  I&#39;ll be managing the source tree.  When changes are received, I will package them and release new versions of Apollo. </p>

<p>What Is It?Currently, a libpurple based IM client which brings AIM, MSN, .Mac, and ICQ to the iPhone. </p>

<p>Can I Help?Of Course You Can!  We may not be focused on it anymore, but you sure as heck can. It is open source and I am now taking up the role of source manager.. </p>

<p>10/1/2007Version 1.0.2 released. </p>

<p>Unicode Support </p>

<p>10/1/2007Version 1.0.1 released. Here we have some much requested bug fixes: </p>

<p>.Mac support is easier to use.  DELETE your .Mac accounts and add them again! Mysterious double size buddies fixes. MSN login problems fixed to the best of our testing. Conversation with hidden buddies and buddies not on buddy list. Login time improvements. Fixed a handful of crashes. </p>

<p>9/23/2007Well, it tooks us longer, but we decided to tweak until it was perfect.  Welcome to ApolloIM 1.0 - here&#39;s our change log. </p>

<p>Added support for DotMac, ICQ, MSN in addition to AIM.  Through libpurple. Buddylist notification of open conversation Multiple account sign on - I&#39;ve been on 8 accounts at once, although, I wouldn&#39;t recommend more than 2-3 active accounts on edge, otherwise it gets slow real quick Sectioned buddy list by accounts Away / Unaway via the pretty green dot in the upper right.  Tap it, turns red, you&#39;re away.  Tap it again, turns green, you&#39;re back. Support for Alias&#39;d buddy names. Support for Status Messages  - shows up in the buddy list Time Stamps in conversation windows Removed Buddyinfo, for now Preparing to add a pane to &quot;Settings&quot; - eliminates need for &quot;Prefs&quot; button for us, will allow extended user options Completely brand new UI. Entire application is brand new, recoded from the bottom up. Stability should be amazingly enhanced. Wifi Keepalive still requires summerboard.   We&#39;ve tested and retested, and while we could have released days ago we chose to keep piling on as many features as we could.  So here you go, the fruit of our labors. </p>

<p>While you&#39;re at it, check out our new homepage - we&#39;re coming up in the world.  We&#39;ll still call our googlecode page home for our svn, but apolloapp will be used to announce more releases and hopefully soon provide more detailed information about features and the like.  Check it out. </p>

<p>9/17/2007Hey guys - just wanted to chime in and say we haven&#39;t forgotten you.  We&#39;re hard at work on 0.2.0, and we&#39;re close to a release.  It&#39;s our most feature packed version yet, better stability, keepalive works pretty well, and we&#39;re adding most of the protocols people have been requesting.  We&#39;re hoping to clear out the issues page :) </p>

<p>As for now, hang tight.  We don&#39;t want to put out any screenshots or anything until our release - we have some surprises in store :) </p>

<p>Until then, feel free to email us - arminius2@gmail.com - and once again, thanks for your support.  Really, you&#39;ve kept us coding and we&#39;ll keep pioneering as long as there is community support.  Thanks guys, really. </p>

<p>-- Quick update - I&#39;ve personally been involved with the iPod touch hacking team, and well, the second we&#39;re inside the touch we&#39;ll have an Apollo client ready. </p>

<p>9/9/2007BETA 0.1.2 is out - here&#39;s the changelog -  </p>

<p>Loads of stability fixes!  Removed options button in favor of using the ringer button.   Ringer button dictates vibrate or playing sounds New Sounds, only send/recv, but much more pleasant Fixed Conversation window sometimes not responding after resume from suspend Fixed &quot;Disconnect not disconnecting&quot; Added Wifi Keep Alive If you are using SummerBoard, the latest version now works with ApolloIM to not turn off   Wifi.  There is no reconnect support yet, but this is a solid feature.  Note: This will drain your battery much faster because Wifi is kept on while in lock while ApolloIM is running.  But it works pretty great and the drain seems to be manageable Does not vibrate on send.  In other news, we&#39;re gearing up for libpurple.  We don&#39;t know when we&#39;ll feel confident to release our work, but we do have a test client that can sign on to aim / msn / jabber.  It&#39;s not pretty yet and not all of the dangly bits are hooked up - but we&#39;re pretty happy with our progress.  Special thanks to the Adium Team as well as Sean Egan for pointing us in the right direction a few times.  There&#39;s no set timeline for when it will be ready, but as soon as we&#39;re sure it&#39;s solid, we will release it.  The release of libpurple will start the 0.2.0 versions. </p>

<p>As soon as we&#39;re sure libpurple is working great, we&#39;ll bump our version up to 1.0 :) </p>

<p>Enjoy the new beta, and please, if you have any feedback - arminius2@gmail.com  - We&#39;re also going to have a site ready for you very soon.   </p>

<p>9/4/2007Released BETA 0.1.1 to fix a couple small things.  Preferences weren&#39;t sticking but should now, and back on Preferences takes you back to the buddy screen.  Badges should work better now. </p>

<p>9/3/2007Well, we&#39;ve released BETA 0.1 - that&#39;s right folks, we&#39;re above Zero.  The stability in this version is far superior, and I believe that it&#39;s actually ready for &quot;Use.&quot;  We&#39;ve piled through the issues and fixed as many bugs as we could have, and for being barely a week old, I think we&#39;re doing amazing things.  We have also just gotten, as of today, libPurple fully compiled and the nullclient/ncurses client (Finch) working, and so you can expect support in the near future for MSN/Yahoo/Jabber/Gtalk and as many others as we can get linked - special thanks to Core &amp; Nightwatch for working hard on that. </p>

<p>Since last week we&#39;ve implemented a host of changes - mostly at the request of people like yourself.  So please keep filing &quot;Issues&quot; and if you&#39;ve got a comment on a build or would like to say thanks - feel free to email the team (emails at the right). </p>

<p>Notable Fixes: -Conversation Windows&#39; scrolling is a lot smoother and works a lot more reliably (Fixed by moving to a UIScroller) </p>

<p>-Defaults back to the send box after sending a message (was the conversation window. Fixed by moving to a UIScroller) </p>

<p>-If you are disconnected, your password is wrong, or you chose to disconnect - it will not close ApolloIM.  You&#39;re free to select another account or change your pass and then reconnect. </p>

<p>Firsts: -First application to implement Edge Keep Alive - found method in NetworkController.h that  should bring Edge up if it&#39;s down as well as keep edge alive while in suspend.  This however does not apply to Wifi yet - wifi is seemingly controlled by Springboard, and when springboard suspends at lockdown it will bring this down.  We&#39;re on the lookout for getting a springboard hack implemented (a la summerboard), and as soon as we get something we&#39;ll implement it asap.  For now, assuming you&#39;ve got plenty of bars of coverage, Edge will stay connected.  I would warn you that there is the chance you will miss a call / text message, but every time I have received a text/call while on ApolloIM (on Edge), it has exited Apollo and allowed me to take the call.  Will require much testing. </p>

<p>-First application to implement vibration.  Admittedly, it&#39;s a dirty hack right now - but our buddy pumpkin in #iphone-uikit has come through and found a way to get vibrate working.  You can turn it on and off (Along with sound!) at your discretion. </p>

<p>Other New Features: -Buddy info works, but isn&#39;t pretty. -Delete button for Accounts -UI Badges like Mail/MobileSMS for unread messages </p>

<p>What sort of works: -Sound is kind of wonky at moment.  For example, if you&#39;re playing a song on the iPod  and you get a message while sound is on, it will pause your song and not resume.  We haven&#39;t figured out yet how to send the notification to turn it back on.  For now, I would recommend that you keep sound off while you intend to listen to your earphones and just use vibrate. </p>

<p>9/1/07Fixed edge / &quot;Generic Error&quot; problems.  Turns out the iPhone&#39;s DNS resolver is royally f&#39;d and the new Firetalk didn&#39;t like it, but I have remedied this for now by just popping the raw IP into the server host field. </p>

<p>This should fix the immediate issues that cropped up from last release.  Notably &quot;Generic Error,&quot; and this will also be the last release  until Monday night where I endeavor to clear out the &quot;Issues&quot; page.  Several dev&#39;s are getting ready to do  branches with sound/vibrate updates and I&#39;m personally gearing up for a real &quot;suspend&quot;.   </p>

<p>Special thanks to the dude at the Apple Store in boulder who had ApolloIM on his phone.  It was really rad seeing that. </p>

<p>Gizmodo, I&#39;m hoping for a &quot;ApolloIM One Week Later:  85% less suck on the road to Beta&quot; Tuesday morning. </p>

<p>9/1/07Wow, 7300 downloads last night.  That&#39;s really nuts.   </p>

<p>Truth be told -.8 was just a quick fix for the buddy list, today I will be releasing a proper implementation (working on it right now, 10am on a Saturday morning).  I would hold off until Early Sunday morning if you haven&#39;t upgraded yet. </p>

<p>8/31/07Negative .8 is up and the buddylist should be fixed and there should be far less crashing.    Before you sign on, I advise you to set your account to inactive, save, then go back and set it as active.   </p>

<p>Note:  Edge does not work in this connect.  It will be fixed Saturday  - Sept 1st - with version negative point seven five.  New firetalk is too fast, interface doesn&#39;t have a chance to come up. </p>

<p>8/30/07Firstly,  I want to thank the person who donated $300 to the new team.  These kind of donations keep me working hard, and now that we have a real team coming together, will keep us focused. If you wish to help out, every little bit helps, and will be used 100% towards materials needed while coding.  Just contact us and we&#39;ll set you up with our paypal information. </p>

<p>Now, on to the news... </p>

<p>Suspend support is partially working.  You can go and use other programs, and ApolloIM will still stay open.   </p>

<p>The main problem with suspend is that the iPhone goes into a low power mode when shoved into your pocket waiting for a call - and this mode will shut off edge / wifi.  Simply pinging the server won&#39;t keep the wifi up, as it seems the kernel does its best to plain unload it.  I don&#39;t know what the prospective fix for this, one idea would be to move to a client/remote daemon, which would mean you would run a client on your home computer which would record all the incoming messages to you and send it over to you (and when your phone goes off, you&#39;d still be on, because the daemon is still running). </p>

<p>Suspend as whole, however, should work while you&#39;re playing music.  If you&#39;re playing a song while ApolloIM is on and in your pocket, it will keep the iphone active enough to keep the program connected.  The trick for me here is to find how exactly Apple does that, and well, I&#39;m on the case. </p>

<p>I&#39;ve also improved the Conversation window, at the cost of making the Send button uglier - if you have problems with the send button, aim for hitting the &quot;text&quot; on the button.  You no longer can type in the main window, and I may release another update very soon to use &quot;text bubbles&quot; like iChat uses.  I have removed the keyboard button in favor of just being able to tap the main view to bring up the keyboard (or you can tap the sendfield at the bottom which,like MobileSMS, will bring up the keyboard). </p>

<p>This will be the last update for a while.  I have been working alone on this project since it&#39;s beginning, but the team has started to come together.  It was kind of funny to see people say &quot;The ApolloIM team&quot; when it was just me, but thanks to my initial release, I&#39;ve gotten some star players to help out.  Notably Dankow who will be working on the interface and keeping code tidy, and Core who has stepped up to help us get libpurple worked out.   If you know libpurple well, and would enjoy helping us integrate it, please send me an email at arminius2@gmail.com . </p>

<p>LibPurple will enable us to have Yahoo, MSN, Jabber, and GTalk support when we get it ready, as well as fix the &quot;Buddy&#39;s not showing up&quot; error.  I suspect my current implementation of libfiretalk is bugged, and I can either work on exchanging it for a different version or get purple working an adding support for the other services.  I&#39;m told one solution could be for you to create a new screen-name and import your buddylist with a &quot;real&quot; client, and then not to change the formatting of any names.  It&#39;s cumbersome, but until we get Libpurple working, it&#39;ll have to do. </p>

<p>8/27/07Fixed suspend support.  ApolloIM will keep running now if you press the homebutton.  SVN is up, binary may be up tonight.</p>

<p>Some of the implemented/planned features/improvements are. </p>

 title : The applicability Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Plugin functionality&#39;application_config&#39; eases project configuring by introducing yaml config file in RAILS_ROOT/config folder and provides handful methods accessing config values based on current rails environment. So, you can have separate sets of configuration properties for each rails environment you use.  </p>

<p>SVN Repositoryhttp://application-config.googlecode.com/svn/ </p>

<p>Installation&gt; ruby ./script/plugin install http://application-config.googlecode.com/svn/tags/application-config </p>

<p>Default configuration fileDuring installation, plugin will create default config in RAILS_ROOT/config/application_config.yml, it looks like the following: </p>

<p>  development: &amp;defaults
<br/>    items_per_page: 25
<br/>    secure_with_basic_auth: false
<br/>    base_url: development.com
<br/>  test:
<br/>    &lt;&lt; ApplicationController
<br/>    def index
<br/>      @base_url = property(:base_url)
<br/>    end
<br/>  endThis will set @items_per_page with value &#39;development.com&#39; if you run that in development environment. </p>

 title : The application-config Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>An application wiki is designed to encourage ordinary users to develop a literacy in building real applications.  In the same way that Wikipedia allows users to collaborate on text, the hope is that an application wiki would let users collaborate on not just words but real behavior. </p>

<p>The framework is loosely based on Ruby on Rails but uses a component pattern where users can author new components and inherit functionality of existing components. </p>

<p>The current framework provides a number of simple applications from instant turnkey chat-rooms to rooms where you can drag windows around and control the layout on the fly. </p>

<p>The ultimate goal is to have a fully transparent programming environment where as much of the environment itself is self-editable by the users. </p>

<p>Ideas here are drawn from Wikipedia, Camping, Hackety Hack, Mousehole, Squeak, Ning, Prototype Windows, PageFlakes and comments from R0ml at OSCON regarding an emerging new literacy. </p>

<p>See </p>

<p>http://appwiki.com 
<br/>for an example. </p>

 title : The aptera Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This project represents a distributed bug tracking and documentation wiki. Distributed is probably a misnomer as its expected that the result will live in the project directory of a project managed by and application like git, bzr, darcs etc. So the distributed version control system will actually provide the distribution while aptera just tries to live in harmony with those systems. Aptera follows the usual unix facility of many small programs that do one thing and do it well. This should allow for easy integration with editors like emacs as well as easy scripting.</p>

 title : The ar-backup Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Latest update: Nov 28 2007 ( patch submitted by Cyril Mougel) </p>

<p>fixed : ar-backup not working properly when the OS isn&#39;t in English (svn issues) fixed : can&#39;t create a backup folder on windows when the revision isn&#39;t defined enhanced : speed has been improved since we are now parsing the local svn files. </p>

<p>Active Record backup is a Rails plugin which lets you backup your database schema and content in a schema.rb file and fixtures.  </p>

<p>Backups are organized by environments and SVN revision. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>ar-backup is compatible with sake http://errtheblog.com/post/6069 
<br/>To install in Rails: </p>

<p>Rails script: </p>

<p> ruby script/plugin install http://ar-backup.googlecode.com/svn/ar-backup  </p>

<p>Piston: </p>

<p> piston import http://ar-backup.googlecode.com/svn/ar-backup vendor/plugins/ar-backup  </p>

<p>SVN: </p>

<p> svn co http://ar-backup.googlecode.com/svn/ar-backup vendor/plugins/ar-backup  </p>

<p>Sake: </p>

<p> sake -i http://ar-backup.googlecode.com/svn/ar-backup/tasks/ar_backup_tasks.sake  </p>

<p>Prerequisites:Your project must be under subversion 
<br/>Usage:rake backup:db:dump               # create a backup folder containing your db schema and content data (see backup/{env}/build{build number}) </p>

<p>rake backup:db:extract_content    # Create YAML fixtures from your DB content </p>

<p>rake backup:db:extract_schema     # Dump the db schema </p>

<p>rake backup:db:load               # load your backed up data from a previous build. rake backup:db:load BUILD=1182 or rake backup:db:load BUILD=1182 DUMP_ENV=production </p>

<p>Backup your database content and schema. (development environment) 
<br/>rake backup:db:dump 
<br/>Do the same thing but with the production environment (note that the previous backup won&#39;t be overwritten) 
<br/>RAILS_ENV=production rake backup:db:dump 
<br/>Restore the database content and schema backed up under BUILD=2547 
<br/>rake backup:db:load BUILD=2547 
<br/>Restore the production database backup into our development db 
<br/>rake backup:db:load BUILD=2547 DUMP_ENV=production  
<br/>Capistrano 2 usage example(you first need to create a backup folder)  </p>

<p>set :backup_dir, &quot;#{deploy_to}/backup&quot; 
<br/>before :deploy do 
<br/>db.backup 
<br/>db.move_backup 
<br/>end 
<br/>namespace :db do 
<br/>desc &#39;create the production database&#39; 
<br/>task :create do 
<br/>run &quot;cd #{current_release} &amp;&amp; rake db:create RAILS_ENV=production&quot; 
<br/>end 
<br/>desc &#39;dump the database schema and content&#39; 
<br/>task :backup do 
<br/>run &quot;cd #{current_release} &amp;&amp; rake backup:db:dump RAILS_ENV=production&quot; 
<br/>end 
<br/>desc &#39;timestamp the backup file&#39; 
<br/>task :move_backup do 
<br/>run &quot;cd #{current_release} &amp;&amp; mv backup/production #{backup_dir}/production#{Time.now.strftime(&quot;%Y-%m-%d%H-%M&quot;)}&quot; 
<br/>end 
<br/>end</p>

 title : The arcanumchs Open Source Project on Open Hub
 title : The archfs Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Anyone who at least once lost his project knows – I personally do - how important it is to create backups. Rdiff-backup (http://www.nongnu.org/rdiff-backup/) allows user to incrementally backup one directory into another. Increments make disk usage relatively low, as only differences between two consecutive backups are stored. This has its drawbacks, however. Although user can access files from most recent backup easily, simply by entering the backup directory, it is much harder to access and browse through older versions. Rdiff-backup allows to access them only by set of instructions, that require precise knowledge of file names and backup times. To investigate creation process of certain project one has to invest a lot of time and energy. This reduces rdiff-backup directory to simple copy of a project rather than repository of all its versions. </p>

<p>Possible solution is to create userspace filesystem based on rdiff-backup repository data. As these information are well and explicitly stored, they can be easily accessed by the filesystem and presented to user in clear and friendly manner. Instead of doing a lot typing and bookkeeping, user will be able to freely browse through any revision of the backed up directory. </p>

<p>The easiest – in my opinion – way to create one, is to use FUSE (Filesystem in userspace - http://fuse.sourceforge.net/) library that allows the developer to focus on high level aspects of the filesystem (e.g. Accessing rdiff-back information and files), while it does all the necessary low level work itself. Since using FUSE does not require root privileges it can be used by any user to create personal filesystem on demand. </p>

<p>As soon as filesystem is correctly mounted, it will provide access to snapshot of the repository for every increment that had been done. Directory structure will be the same as the backed up directory at the time of the increment. Any file added to the repository at the will be accessible, yet only the accessed files will be replicated, so disk space usage stays low. </p>

<p>Latest version of archfs works with rdiff-backup 1.0.x and 1.1.x. </p>

<p>Idea for this filesystem was first presented by Lukasz Sznuk from University of Warsaw as one of the projects for course in Operating Systems.</p>
 summary : <p>Archimedes MVC Framework inspired by Ruby on Rails.</p>

 title : The arcwelder Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>UPDATEGFT technique works on Archos 604, 605, and 705 wifi models You can download a kitchen sink rootfs build (everything I could get to compile out of the Archos GPL tarball out of the box) from http://www.remix.net/archos/ax605_rootfs.tar.bz2 You can enable scp/sftp by either fixing the config to reference sftp/ssh from /tmp/ssh, or just hex edit the defaults in sshd. I haven&#39;t made this change in arcwelder-1.0.zip, this change will be made and a new archive will be uploaded (soon?). WARNINGThe techniques and software provided in this project are dangerous to the well-being of your Archos if you don&#39;t know what you&#39;re doing. If you&#39;re not comfortable in a Unix/Linux environment, DO NOT USE THIS SOFTWARE. You will brick your Archos and have nobody to blame but yourself.  </p>

<p>In using these techniques and software you assume all risk and hold harmless the arcwelder project and myself for any damages real or imagined. Don&#39;t go crying to Archos either, it&#39;s not their fault. </p>

<p>To make things even more interesting, I&#39;ve haven&#39;t tested things rigorously. Scared yet? You should be! </p>

<p>Nathan Ramella, n ar @ h u sh.com </p>

<p>SummaryThrough a technique dubbed &quot;Go Fighting Tabby!&quot;, or GFT for short, you can gain root access on an Archos 605 wifi running 1.7.13 firmware and execute arbitrary programs in its embedded Linux environment.  </p>

<p>This is the first step to gain access to the running Linux operating system, which until now has not been possible. </p>

<p>Using the GFT technique, you can install the &#39;ARCwelder&#39; package which will allow you to ssh into the Archos 605 wifi and run unix commands from a shell.  </p>

<p>Currently ARCwelder only provides an ssh package, however in time more packages may be included as they are tested and verified as working, some customization is necessary to ensure that they work on the embedded system, so the term &#39;hack&#39; is definitely applicable. </p>

<p>Go Fighting Tabby! Technique ExplainedThe GFT technique is pretty simple, after auditing the GPL tarball from Archos, I found a script named &#39;smbpasswdhelper&#39;. </p>

<p>smbpasswdhelper </p>

<p>#!/bin/sh</p>

<p>if test $# -ne 2
<br/>then
<br/>        echo &quot;usage: $0 account password&quot;
<br/>        exit 1
<br/>fi</p>

<p>/opt/usr/bin/smbpasswd -x $1</p>

<p>/opt/usr/bin/smbpasswd -s -a $1 &lt;&lt; EOF
<br/>$2
<br/>$2
<br/>EOFWhat got me interested was that it didn&#39;t quote $2, I figured $1 would be hard-coded to whatever the smb user is for connecting (guest maybe?), so I started poking it a bit. As it turns out, that wasn&#39;t even necessary, as I believe the avos application is doing a straight system call without sanitizing the user supplied password string.  </p>

<p>If you&#39;re at all familiar with shell commands, the prospect of an unsanitized string being used in a system() call is pretty attractive from a hacker&#39;s perspective. It means by using a little shell trickery you can launch your own command. </p>

<p>But how do you use this script? </p>

<p>That&#39;s the nice part, the Archos UI has provided you a text box to type in whatever you want for the &#39;password&#39; under the wifi settings, after you&#39;ve connected to a wifi network. You can set the password and launch an smb server, in doing so the smbpasswdhelper script is run (along with your hijack command). Even better, it runs your command as root, so you&#39;ve got full privileges from the start. </p>

<p>GFT Technique AppliedConnect to a wifi network From the top level of the avos app, goto your wireless settings again, this time you should see your IP address and other network configuration information. Scroll to the bottom and select Wireless File Server.. Setup your Samba info as you like, but select the Password setting to bring up the keyboard UI. Change the password to &quot;1;ls -laR / &gt;/mnt/data/Data/file_list.txt&quot; , include the quotes, that&#39;s important Click/Run Enable File Server After a couple seconds, the UI will notify you that the fileserver has started, that means your command has run.  Pop back up to the top level of the UI Select the Files icon by double clicking it Browse to Data, you should see file_list.txt, you should be able to read the file by clicking it (If you have the Opera web browser, if you don&#39;t, you&#39;ll need to attach your Archos to a computer and read the file that way), inside file_list.txt will be a full directory listing of your Archos device. You can run any supported Unix command using this technique, this gives you direct access to the &quot;hidden&quot; Linux partitions. This technique can be used to run / install other scripts, but if you install ARCwelder, you can just ssh in and do it that way. The Archos is set to power down the wireless whenever it can, so you may get disconnected if there&#39;s no activity. Since the archos support library is included in the GPL tarball, this may have something in it to hard-code longer timeouts. Installing ARCwelderDownload ARCwelder-1.0.zip  Connect your Archos 605 wifi to your computer, select hard drive mode Mount your Archos on your computer Unzip the contents of ARCwelder-1.0.zip into /Data/, this will make a directory named &#39;arcwelder&#39; and populate it with the necessary files. When complete you can verify this step by checking /Data/arcwelder/ and make sure that your file list matches the MANIFEST.txt file. Copy /Data/arcwelder/id_arcwelder into ~/.ssh/ on your client machine if you&#39;re using OSX or Linux, if you&#39;re using Windows download PuTTY and use that. id_arcwelder is a password-less RSA key. For instructions on using PuTTY check out the wiki entry How_to_use_RSA_keys_with_Putty DO NOT install id_arcwelder.pub into your ~/.ssh/ directory.  Use the GFT technique to run this command &quot;1;/bin/sh -x /mnt/data/Data/arcwelder/install&quot; , if you have trouble and need some debugging information you can GFT &quot;1;/bin/sh -x /mnt/data/Data/arcwelder/install 1&gt;/mnt/data/Data/stdout.txt 2&gt;/mnt/data/Data/stderr.txt&quot; , this will save both the standard output and standard errors into files so you can see what happened. A typical &#39;good&#39; stderr file will look something like this: + mkdir /tmp/ssh/
<br/>+ mkdir /tmp/empty
<br/>+ chmod 755 /tmp/empty
<br/>+ cp /mnt/data/Data/ssh/authorized_keys /mnt/data/Data/ssh/fix /mnt/data/Data/ssh/id_archos /mnt/data/Data/ssh/id_arcwelder.pub /mnt/data/Data/ssh/sftp-server /mnt/data/Data/ssh/ssh-keysign /mnt/data/Data/ssh/ssh_banner /mnt/data/Data/ssh/ssh_config /mnt/data/Data/ssh/ssh_host_dsa_key /mnt/data/Data/ssh/ssh_host_dsa_key.pub /mnt/data/Data/ssh/ssh_host_key /mnt/data/Data/ssh/ssh_host_key.pub /mnt/data/Data/ssh/ssh_host_rsa_key /mnt/data/Data/ssh/ssh_host_rsa_key.pub /mnt/data/Data/ssh/sshd /mnt/data/Data/ssh/sshd_config /tmp/ssh/
<br/>+ cd /tmp/ssh
<br/>+ chmod 755 authorized_keys fix id_arcwelder id_arcwelder.pub sftp-server ssh-keysign ssh_banner ssh_config ssh_host_dsa_key ssh_host_dsa_key.pub ssh_host_key ssh_host_key.pub ssh_host_rsa_key ssh_host_rsa_key.pub sshd sshd_config
<br/>+ chmod 4711 ssh-keysign
<br/>+ chmod 600 /tmp/ssh/ssh_host_dsa_key /tmp/ssh/ssh_host_key /tmp/ssh/ssh_host_rsa_key
<br/>+ chmod 600 /tmp/ssh/authorized_keys
<br/>+ chmod 644 /tmp/ssh/id_arcwelder.pub /tmp/ssh/ssh_host_dsa_key.pub /tmp/ssh/ssh_host_key.pub /tmp/ssh/ssh_host_rsa_key.pub
<br/>+ /tmp/ssh/sshd -f /tmp/ssh/sshd_configUsing ARCwelderConnect to your wifi network using the instructions found on page 42 of the Archos User Manual.  Use the GFT technique to run the install script.  Once ARCwelder is installed, and you have installed the private RSA key on your client machine, connect your Archos 605 wifi to your wireless connection, Find_your_Archos_IP_address and then run &#39;ssh -l root &#39;, you should be greeted with the following banner and login prompt: $ ssh -l root 192.168.1.120
<br/>                             _     _

 summary : <p>Arid POJOs is a framework for simplifying POJO application development. </p>

<p>Automatic Spring Bean GenerationArid POJOs provides a custom Spring/XML namespace that scans a package hierarchy and generate bean definitions for the classes or interfaces that it finds. The classes and interfaces can be filtered by an AspectJ type pattern, which supports various criteria including name matching, annotations, and subtypes. The generated beans use autowiring. Here is a simple example. </p>

<p>Dynamic Generic DAOsArid POJOs can also generate DAO implementations from an interface using a Grails GORM/Rails Active Record like mechanism. Here is an example interface: </p>

<br/>	Customer findUsingSomeStrangeNamedQuery(String firstName, String lastName);
<br/>}Arid POJOs will generate a proxy, which implements this interface. The findByCustomerId() method is turned into Criteria Query, which searches on the customerId property, and the findUsingSomeStrangeNamedQuery() method ends up calling a named query.  summary : <p>Ariel intends to assist in extracting information from semi-structured

 summary : <p>This is a naive Bayesian text classifier that, given a bit of text can tell you the posterior probability (returned as a log likelihood) that it comes from each of the standard scientific article sections (Introduction, Methods, Results, Discussion). </p>

<p>What do we mean by a bit of text, well anything you want really, from a few words to a whole article, you decide on the boundaries. </p>

<p>You can use it to:Pull out all the bits of text from an article that are from your chosen section. Score each bit of text in 4 dimensions (i.e. how introductory, methodological, results-based or conclusionary it is) which may be useful for finding similar text. Use it to create training data etc. This project contains:A local version of the classifier, for better performance (see Downloads, or choose a version from the downloads list to the right) Links and info on how to access the web service interface to the classifier (see below) Example client software Ruby and Perl for accessing the web service from your code (see Downloads) Some Taverna workflows that give a demonstration of how to use the classifier web service (coming soon) The training data (useful for error analyses) datastore.dump A user guide for the web service (coming soon) Some javadoc describing the code for the web service interface and its associated bean classes. ArticleSectionClassifier-1.0-javadoc.zip Test the classifierYou can test the classifier through your browser here </p>

<p>Download the classifierDownloads are all listed here or you can see the featured downloads on the right hand side of this page.  </p>

<p>SOAP/WSDL Web ServiceThe wsdl document for the web service is here and you can test it directly through your browser here.  You can also download local clients in Java, Perl and Ruby for accessing the web service. </p>

<p>Using the classifier in JavaFirst you must include the ArticleSectionClassifer.jar file in your classpath.  Secondly it is best to increase the memory allocated by the Java executable using the -Xmx Java VM argument, I usually suggest -Xmx256m.  Then you can use the classifier in few lines of code. </p>

<p>String textToClassify = &quot;classify this text&quot;;
<br/>ArticleSectionClassifier classifier = new ArticleSectionClassifier();
<br/>String classifiedAs = classifiers.classifyText(textToClassify);
<br/>System.out.println(classifiedAs);If you want more detailed output try  </p>

<p>String textToClassify = &quot;classify this text&quot;;
<br/>ClassificationInput input = new ClassificationInput(textToClassify);
<br/>ArticleSectionClassifier classifier = new ArticleSectionClassifier();
<br/>ClassificationResult result = classifier.classifyText(input);
<br/>System.out.println(result);Source codeDetails on getting the source code for this project can be found by clicking on the &#39;Source&#39; tab above or by clicking here.  You can also download an archive of the source from here. The source is uploaded as part of a Netbeans project, which can be opened directly into Netbeans or imported into Eclipse or most other IDEs. </p>

It&#39;s very likely that something won&#39;t work, but its also likely that i&#39;ve encountered it before and will know how to fix it, therefore if you have a problem, let me know.</p>

 title : The artoo Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>ArtOO got its name from a RoR localization plugin I helped develop with the Macau.com IT team. We decided to call that plugin &#39;C3PO&#39; named after the Star Wars translation/protocol droid. As I tried to mimic or replicate the C3PO plugin using PHP, I came up with the ArtOO project. Most of ArtOO&#39;s features are RoR inspired, however, some of ArtOO&#39;s codes had been just a rewrite of some old PHP4 classes I&#39;ve written as far back as the year 2002. A great deal of codes had also been written since 2005.</p>
 summary : <p>What is AS-HIVE? </p>

<p>AS-HIVE allows developers to rapidly build applications and games that rely on state, event, and load management of external media files. </p>

<p>We&#39;d like to foster a collective of creative people who design and develop primarily using Adobe&#39;s Flash. We encourage input and participation from all ranges of people who code in Actionscript. </p>

<p>Hard core developers may be interested to know that AS-HIVE is built on a state-based MVC framework but you don&#39;t have to be a hard core developer to use it.  </p>

<p>Intermediate developers who don&#39;t wish to advance the framework can try the samples so that one can see how to save time and energy allowing AS-HIVE to handle loading your external assets like xml, pngs, flvs and mp3s. AS-HIVE also helps you animate screens by creating sequences that build up and tear down before moving to the next state.  </p>

<p>By integrating other open source projects like Tweener and Papervision3D, AS-HIVE offers a robust and reliable mechanism for manipulating 2D and 3D content allowing the developer to focus on architecture and flow. </p>

<p>How do I learn about AS-HIVE? </p>

<p>The best way to learn HIVE is to ask a lot of questions and join our discussion group. </p>

<p>as-docs </p>

 title : The as3-youtube-data-api Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>IntroductionThis library provides an easy-to-use set of wrapper classes to consume YouTube Data API Web Services. You can: </p>

<p>search for videos by keywords, tags, and categories get access to the standard streams (for most popular videos by different criterias) get a persons full profile information get a video&#39;s comments get a video&#39;s responses get a person&#39;s favorites get a person&#39;s playlists get a person&#39;s subscriptions retreive a playlist A Solution! (2008-04-22)Read this blog post to see how I&#39;ve decided to circumvent AS3&#39;s un-RESTful-ness :  http://blog.martinlegris.com/?p=92 . This is good news, within a week you will have access to the full scope of the youtube data api! (except uploading videos... which will come later). </p>

<p>Important information about supporting the new featuresI have tried, a month ago when the new API rollout happened, to implement the new features offered. However I ran into limitations of AS3 &amp; Flash CS3. Here are the details: http://code.google.com/p/as3-youtube-data-api/wiki/LimitationsOfCS3 </p>

<p>DetailsThe library is based on a singleton Client called YouTubeClient.  It provides feeds and iterators to go through the information received from the YouTube Data API.  These iterators return hard-typed data objects which you can explore easily using your auto-complete IDE such as FlashDevelop, Flex IDE, Eclipse w/FDT, Intellij Idea or other. Each request sent through is identified by a requestId which you can use to filter the different responses you receive, ensuring you do manipulate the expected data. Tutorials &amp; Samples2008-03-28 A new tutorial was posted on the google code website here: http://code.google.com/support/bin/answer.py?answer=92715&amp;topic=12359. The first tutorial was posted here: http://blog.martinlegris.com/?p=83 Some explanations on which events are thrown in which context by YouTubeClient can be found here: http://blog.martinlegris.com/?p=84 Another sample, this one to consume a standard feed is shown here: http://blog.martinlegris.com/?p=81 Help NeededAlthough i&#39;ve done a lot of testing, I realize it can be buggy. I would also need some help to document this beast of 35+ classes. If anyone is interested please let me (Martin) know. Hope you enjoy it! </p>

 title : The as3bots Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>OverviewThis project aims to provide an API to create a virtual robot battle game. ActionScripters will be able to code their own bots to compete against everyone else&#39;s in a Flash environment. </p>

<p>The idea is to have the arena, rules and a base bot created to allow beginners or advanced coders to easily build AI-based robots. </p>

<p>Once it is up and running, the idea is to build a bot that manipulates the data that it can acquire from the Game in the most optimum and efficient way - a really good way of learning AS3 and/or best practices. The info that can be gained from the Game will be limited for each bot, so programmers will need to choose which areas to specialise in. As the bot progresses in the ranks it will be able to gain more information, so its abilities can be extended. </p>

<p>This is a shared project, where anyone can contribute ideas and/or code. </p>

<p>Phase 2 and 3 are complete, with the latter integrating the motor2 physics engine. </p>

<p>Future PhasesWe already have many ideas for future phases of this project. These are viewable on the wiki. </p>

<p>A FlashBrighton Project</p>
 summary : <p>As3cAs3c is a bytecode compiler for the AVM2 written in C#. </p>

<p>FeaturesIt allows you to... </p>

<p>compile inline assemlber instructions written in in ActionScript 3 while maintining full debugging capabilities. compile pure bytecode into a precompiled output format. inject precompiled files into a SWF by replacing or creating methods. </p>

<p>As3c works great with Mono on Linux and OS X. You do not even have to recompile it. </p>

<p>Syntax exampleHello worldThis example is equivalent to a simple trace(&#39;Hello World!&#39;). </p>

<p>package  
<br/>{
<br/>	import flash.display.Sprite;
<br/>	
<br/>	import de.popforge.asm.Op;
<br/>	import de.popforge.asm.__asm;		</p>

<p>	/**
<br/>	 * Hello World example using As3c inline asm syntax.
<br/>	 *
<br/>	 * @author Joa Ebert
<br/>	 */
<br/>	public class Main extends Sprite 
<br/>	{
<br/>		public function Main()
<br/>		{
<br/>			__asm(
<br/>				Op.findPropertyStrict(&#39;public::trace&#39;),
<br/>				Op.pushString(&#39;Hello World!&#39;),
<br/>				Op.callPropertyVoid(&#39;public::trace&#39;, 1)´
<br/>			);
<br/>		}
<br/>	}
<br/>}New possibilitiesWhen using asm you can define labels wherever you want. You can also jump to labels from any point in your code. This opens completly new possibilities as you can see. Although this one might be a little bit confusing ;) </p>

<p>package  
<br/>{
<br/>	import flash.display.Sprite;
<br/>	
<br/>	import de.popforge.asm.Op;
<br/>	import de.popforge.asm.__asm;		</p>

<p>	/**
<br/>	 * Asm example for new possibilities when using labels and inline asm.
<br/>	 * 
<br/>	 * @author Joa Ebert
<br/>	 */
<br/>	public class Main extends Sprite 
<br/>	{
<br/>		public function Main()
<br/>		{
<br/>			if (true === true)
<br/>			{
<br/>				__asm(Op.jump(&#39;.else&#39;));
<br/>				__asm(&#39;.if:&#39;);
<br/>				
<br/>				trace(&#39;Hello if!&#39;);
<br/>			}
<br/>			else
<br/>			{
<br/>				__asm(&#39;.else:&#39;);
<br/>				
<br/>				trace(&#39;Hello else!&#39;);
<br/>				
<br/>				__asm(Op.jump(&#39;.if&#39;));
<br/>			}
<br/>		}
<br/>	}
<br/>}AlternativesIf you are familiar with the haXe language you might want to take a look at hxASM. An ActionScript 2 alternative is flasm.</p>

 title : The as3corelib Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>As3 Crypto is a cryptography library written in Actionscript 3 that provides several common algorithms. This version also introduces a TLS engine (TLS is commonly known as SSL.) </p>

<p>Protocols: TLS 1.0 support (partial) Certificates: X.509 Certificate parsing and validation, built-in Root CAs. Public Key Encryption: RSA (encrypt/decrypt, sign/verify) Secret Key Encryption: AES, DES, 3DES, BlowFish, XTEA, RC4 Confidentiality Modes: ECB, CBC, CFB, CFB8, OFB, CTR Hashing Algorithms: MD2, MD5, SHA-1, SHA-224, SHA-256 Paddings available: PKCS#5, PKCS#1 type 1 and 2 Other Useful Stuff: HMAC, Random, TLS-PRF, some ASN-1/DER parsing The library is offered under the BSD license, and include several derivative works from Java, C and javascript sources. Check the LICENSE.txt file for a list of contributors. </p>

<p>You can look at a demo of the functionality of the library. It&#39;s built with Flex 2. It includes a unit test tab, and a benchmark tab. </p>

<p>This is what the benchmark tab outputs on my computer (Athlon64 2Ghz): </p>

 summary : <p>This project has moved. It is now part of the Cannonball project.</p>
 summary : <p>AS3Dmod is a cross-engine modifier library in AS3.AS3Dmod is a library of modifiers for 3d objects. A modifier is an function used to modify a 3d object. Currently AS3Dmod contains 7 modifiers: </p>

<p>Bend - bends on object along an axis Noise - deforms an object in a random manner Skew - skews an object along one or more axes Taper - http://www.kxcad.net/autodesk/3ds_max/Autodesk_3ds_Max_9_Reference/taper_modifier.html Bloat - Bloats the mesh by forcing vertices out of specified sphere Perlin - Generates a perlin noise bitmap and displaces vertices based on the color value of each pixel of the noise map Twist - twists the mesh around it&#39;s center point AS3Dmod also features an abstract layer and a simple plug-in architecture that allows the modifiers to work with most of the popular Flash 3d engines. </p>

<p>Current version 0.2. Features include: </p>

<p>7 modifiers as listed above a framework for creating static and animated modifier stacks 4 plug-ins for the most popular 3d engines: Pv3d, Away3d, Sandy3d and Alternativa3d a simple demo for each engine Documentation (in progress) can be found here: http://www.everydayflash.com/flash/as3dmod/doc/</p>

<br/>	
<br/>Table structures is: </p>

<p>CREATE TABLE `users` (
<br/>  `id` int(5) NOT NULL auto_increment,
<br/>  `username` varchar(255) NOT NULL,
<br/>  `password` varchar(255) NOT NULL,
<br/>  `fname` varchar(255) NOT NULL,
<br/>  `lname` varchar(255) NOT NULL,
<br/>  PRIMARY KEY  (`id`)
<br/>) ENGINE=InnoDB  DEFAULT CHARSET=latin1;</p>

 summary : <p>AS3GIF lets you play and encode animated GIF&#39;s with ActionScript 3</p>
 summary : <p>Whyas3Glue gives Flash, Flex and AIR applications physical interaction capabilities. </p>

<p>Detailsas3Glue is an ActionScript 3 library that enables communication between Flash/Flex/AIR applications and Arduino boards. It can together with one or several Arduino boards be used to monitor sensors (such as rotary encoders and motion detectors), control actuators (such as LEDs and motors) and interface other electronics (such as RFID readers) from Flash, Flex and AIR applications.  </p>

<p>The library includes Arduino sketches and ActionScript 3 code examples as well as the Standard Firmata v2 Arduino firmware and a serial proxy. </p>

<p>Firmata 1.0 vs Firmata 2.0The latest version of this library was developed for Firmata 2.0.  Arduino 0012 and later are distributed with Firmata 2.0. Earlier versions shipped with Firmata 1.0, which is NOT compatible with 2.0. If your project requires Firmata 1.0, you can find an earlier version of as3Glue the downloads section, although we do not recommend it for new projects. </p>

<p>If you are comfortable with Subversion, /trunk/ is compatible with Firmata 2.0, while /branches/firmata1/ contains the library for Firmata 1.0. </p>

<p>FeaturesMonitor and control digital and analog pins on Arduino boards from ActionScript 3 application without any Arduino programming. </p>

<p>Quickly send and receive data to and from Arduino boards using the efficient Standard Firmata protocol.  </p>

<p>Interface multiple Arduino boards. </p>

<p>Problems?Please read the FAQ first. </p>

<p>Licenseas3Glue is an open source library licensed under the MIT license.  </p>

<p>RoadmapAuthorsBjoern Hartmann, http://bjoern.org/</p>

<p>FAQIf anybody from Adobe is reading this: Please add outputProgress event to Socket. (This is the same behavior as outputProgress event in FileStream.)  Otherwise it is impossible to determine the ouput progress on socket writes.. see http://rel.me/2008/1/17/socket-output-progress-in-air for more info.   </p>

<p>Everyone else: Vote for the fix! </p>

<p>Common questions: </p>

<p>In order to use flash.net.Socket in a Flash sandbox environment, you need to have a flash socket policy server. (AIR does not have this restriction.) Look at http://www.adobe.com/devnet/flashplayer/articles/socket_policy_files.html. To debug in the environment, I would use a standalone flash debug player with logging configured and you will see it attempt to connect to flash socket policy server at port 843. Because of this restriction, this library might be more suited for AIR apps. HTTPS doesn&#39;t always work. There are some minor bugs with the as3crypto library, so for example https at yahoo and yahoo owned domains (like delicious) don&#39;t currently work. </p>

<p>The goals for this project are: </p>

<p>Learn the HTTP protocol by trying to implement a client. Use AS3Crypto TLSSocket support for implementing HTTPS. Use it as a replacement for Flash&#39;s URLRequest/URLStream API. Support the Flash and AIR runtimes. </p>

<p>WorkingGET, HEAD, PUT, POST, DELETE multipart/form-data (PUT and POST) HTTPS support using AS3Crypto TLS Post with application/x-www-form-urlencoded Reading chunked (Transfer-Encoding) Next to implementThe other http verbs Connection keep-alive gzip compression ...</p>

<p>Example code: </p>

<p>import be.wellconsidered.services.WebService;
<br/>import be.wellconsidered.services.Operation;</p>

<p>import be.wellconsidered.services.events.OperationEvent;</p>

<p>var ws = new WebService(&quot;http://www.webservicex.net/WeatherForecast.asmx?wsdl&quot;);
<br/>var op:Operation = new Operation(ws);</p>

<p>op.addEventListener(OperationEvent.COMPLETE, onResult);
<br/>op.addEventListener(OperationEvent.FAILED, onFault);</p>

<p>op.GetWeatherByPlaceName(&quot;new york&quot;);  </p>

<p>function onResult(e:OperationEvent):void { trace(e.data); }
<br/>function onFault(e:OperationEvent):void { trace(e.data); }</p>

 title : The asset-fury Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This is Not a Working VersionThis plugin tries to bring in the best of attachment_fu and is_attachment into one plugin with much more flexibility in thumbnail managment. </p>

<p>Wether attachment_fu or is_attachment asset and their generated thumbnail are much to tightly coupled in my opinion. </p>

<p>The basic idea is to be able to do this when you want to add a none standard thumbnail to your asset without recreating the hole set of thumbnails (with attachment_fu you need to tweak options to do that) : </p>

<p>@asset = Asset.find_by_name(&#39;my_cat_in_the_washing_machine.jpg&#39;)
<br/>@image = Image.new(:medium=&gt;&#39;150x&#39;}
<br/>@asset &lt;&lt; @image
<br/>@asset.saveOr you may wish to update a given thumbnail individually :  </p>

<p>@image = Image.find(123)
<br/>@image.update()</p>

<p>Issues Resolved in this release: &amp;nbsp;Issue #36&amp;nbsp;, &amp;nbsp;Issue #43&amp;nbsp;, &amp;nbsp;Issue #44&amp;nbsp;, &amp;nbsp;Issue #45&amp;nbsp;, &amp;nbsp;Issue #46&amp;nbsp;  </p>

 title : The asterisk-bsd Open Source Project on Open Hub

<p>Our objective is to facilitate Asterisk support for BSD flavors of Unix, including FreeBSD, NetBSD, OpenBSD, and Mac OS X. </p>

<p>This site is intended to be a clearing house for BSD platform support for the Asterisk VOIP pbx.  It allows developers to more directly share changes to the Asterisk source code that solve issues specific to BSD Unix. </p>

<p>We also intend to collaborate on a group of ports which one day will be inserted into the FreeBSD ports tree. </p>

 title : The async-msgcomp Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Asynchronous messaging allows components to communicate in a robust and reliable manner. In particular sending a message is a non-blocking operation. This means that a receiver of the message cannot directly effect the sender. Compare this to synchronous messaging where the sender is blocked until the receiver decides to return. </p>

<p>The goal of this project is to implement a light weight, robust and reliable asynchronous messaging scheme that supports inter and intra process communication within the same &quot;computer&quot; as well as inter-device communication. In addition, it is to be OS and language agnostic. </p>

<p>I can be reached at @.com </p>

<p>Cheers </p>

<p>Wink Saville</p>
 title : The asynchronous Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>AynchronousNow you can make any method in one of your models asynchronous.  For example,  </p>

<p>class TestRecord &lt; ActiveRecord::Base    </p>

<p>after_save :an_alert 
<br/>   def an_alert 
<br/>logger.info &#39;We could now asynchronously send an email to tons of people with this alert.&#39; 
<br/>end 
<br/>asynchronous :an_alert 
<br/>end </p>

<p>That&#39;s it, just install the plugin, add a &#39;QueuedMethods&#39; table (follow my migration script), and add the &#39;asynchronous :symbol&#39; part below where you declare the method you are making asynchronous.  I&#39;ve included a migration script in the db folder to use for the QueuedMethods table.  </p>

<p>To process your queue just set up a cron job using the script runner: </p>

<p>&#39;script/runner &#39;MethodQueue.process&#39; -e production&#39; </p>

<p>This is still in its first draft, but working under the conditions shown in the tests.  Please feel free though to hack at it an make it better.  I think it&#39;s a pretty useful tool.  But a couple things I don&#39;t like:  </p>

<p>1) What&#39;s the standard way these days to create a table a plugin depends on?  Probably not in the install.rb in case there is a name conflict?  </p>

<p>2) The &#39;asynchronous&#39; part has to be declared below the method declaration.  Is there anyway to make it agnostic of the method declaration location? </p>

<p>TestingIf you want to test, you need to have a test table for the test model setup in the database.  I included a mysql.sql file to create that table in the test/fixtures dir.  Then you can just run &#39;rake&#39;, in your RAILS_PROJ/vendor/plugins/asynchronous. </p>

<p>Major ThanksChris Eppstein provided a great patch that got rid of race condition the original plugin had.  This makes it truly useful for most jobs people need something like this for.  Thanks man! </p>

<p>-Nate http://www.inklingmarkets.com</p>

 title : The aszip Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>ASZip lets you generate ZIP files from ActionScript 3. </p>

<p>Here comes ASZip to generate Zip files from scratch with some files and folders into it. </p>

<p>This first version is using the native gzip (Deflate) compression from the flash.utils.Bytearray.compress() method, more compression algorithms will be added later like PPMD or Bzip2 and more. </p>

<p>To generate a zip file, with a text file and a PNG file, you would do : </p>

<p>// create the Zip file, first param : compression method
<br/>var myZip:ASZip = new ASZip (CompressionMethod.GZIP);
<br/>// create a flash.display.BitmapData
<br/>var myStevie:Stevie = new Stevie (0, 0);
<br/>// encode it as a PNG
<br/>var bytes:ByteArray = PNGEnc.encode (myStevie);
<br/>// create a text stream
<br/>var txt:ByteArray = new ByteArray();
<br/>// write some text into it
<br/>txt.writeUTFBytes(&quot;Hello there !!&quot;);
<br/>// add a pics folder
<br/>myZip.addDirectory (&quot;pics/&quot;);
<br/>// then a text folder
<br/>myZip.addDirectory (&quot;text/&quot;);
<br/>// pass the PNG stream and specify a file name and location
<br/>myZip.addFile (bytes, &quot;pics/stevie.png&quot;);
<br/>// pass the text stream and specify a file name and location
<br/>myZip.addFile (txt, &quot;text/story.txt&quot;);
<br/>// add a comment
<br/>myZip.addComment (&quot;A comment !&quot;);
<br/>// generate final Zip file
<br/>var myZipFile:ByteArray = myZip.saveZIP ( Method.LOCAL );</p>

 title : The atlas-addon Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Atlas, a World of Warcraft instance map browser Copyright 2005 - 2009 Dan Gilbert Email me at loglow@gmail.com About AtlasFor some reason, Blizzard decided to include beautiful maps for every area of Azeroth except instances. You can still see the area surrounding you in the minimap when you&#39;re in an instance, but never the overall layout of the entire dungeon. This is where Atlas comes in. The core of Atlas is basically an image viewer. However, it&#39;s the images that come with Atlas that make it worthwhile: a map for every instance in the game. Furthermore, the maps are marked with the locations of bosses and other points of interest. Atlas also includes maps of battlegrounds, dungeon locations, flight points, and outdoor raid bosses. </p>

<p>After installing Atlas, you&#39;ll notice a new icon on the minimap that looks like part of a little globe (you can right-click the icon to drag it around the minimap&#39;s frame). Click this icon to open up the main Atlas window, which displays the maps and legend. You can alternatively use the slash-command /atlas. The drop-downs at the top of the window enable you to navigate between the maps. You can also drag the Atlas window around the screen. Lock it in place with the little lock button in the upper-right corner. </p>

<p>At the bottom of the legend is a small text-entry field as well as Search and Reset buttons. Type part of a word or name in the box and click the Search button, and the legend&#39;s entries are reduced to only those that match your text. Note that the search is performed only on the entries for the current map, not all the entries in the database. While not so useful for instances with only a few entries like Ragefire Chasm, the search comes in handy when there are a ton of entries, like for Blackrock Depths or the AtlasMajorCities plug-in. If you want to get the whole list back, just click Reset. </p>

<p>ConfigurationAtlas has a few simple options, accessible from the Options button in the upper-right corner of the main window, or with the slash-command /atlas options. A few of the settings aren&#39;t very self-explanatory so here&#39;s some more information about them. &quot;Auto-Select Instance Map&quot; detects the instance that you&#39;re in when you open Atlas, and then automatically switches to the appropriate map. This feature doesn&#39;t work in instances that have more than one map, like Blackrock Spire, Dire Maul, or many of the Outland instances. In this case, Atlas remembers the last map you had open. &quot;Right-Click for World Map&quot; makes the World Map open when you right-click anywhere on the Atlas window. This is useful when you want to quickly switch from Atlas to the World Map. &quot;Clamp Window to Screen&quot; makes it so that you can&#39;t drag the Atlas window off the edge of the screen. The rest of the options are pretty straightforward. The Reset Position button is useful if the Atlas window ever gets dragged completely off-screen and you can&#39;t get it back. </p>

<p>Atlas PluginsAtlas has a built-in plugin system allowing for the easy addition of map packs. In fact, Atlas ships with four of these plugins (for battlegrounds, dungeon locations, flight points, and outdoor raid bosses). If you&#39;re interested in making your own Atlas map pack, I suggest you start with one of these four as a guide. You can contact me or post on the Atlas forums if you need help, however I suggest you do as much research as possible beforehand. Furthermore, there are several Atlas plugins that do more than simply provide additional maps. AtlasLoot provides a loot table for each boss, and AtlasQuest displays the quests associated with each instance. Note that I don&#39;t develop these plugins myself; they have their own project leads. </p>

<p>Before InstallingAny previous versions of Atlas must be deleted prior to installation. Atlas plugins (AtlasLoot, AtlasQuest, etc.) designed for any version of Atlas prior to this one must be deleted. Map packs supplied by Daviesh for Atlas 1.8.6 must be deleted prior to installation (they&#39;re unnecessary now anyway). How to InstallUnzip the package into your World of Warcraft folder. Your zip software must preserve directory structures. If you&#39;re having trouble, please visit the Atlas FAQ: http://www.atlasmod.com/phpBB3/viewtopic.php?t=3 IntegrationLibDataBroker (LDB) Titan Panel myAddOns CTMod Cosmos Websitehttp://www.atlasmod.com/ ContactName: Dan Gilbert Email: loglow@gmail.com AIM: dan5981 LicenseAtlas is released under the GNU General Public License (GPL). For the full license text please see: gpl-v2-enUS.txt</p>

 title : The attachbot Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Intro </p>

<p>This is a simple and intuitive application designed for you to upload pictures and PDF attachments to RYGH BBS (http://bbs.fudan.edu.cn).  This application is inspired by tyllr&#39;s Upload Helper (http://homepage.fudan.edu.cn/~tyllr/uh/index.htm) </p>

<p>Running RequirementsMac OS X 10.4 or later versions. If you are using OSX 10.4, please download the tiger version. </p>

<p>FeaturesMulti-threaded uploading. preview what you are uploading with one-click Quick Look. User Account management, doesn&#39;t have to manually login each time. Keep the list of board you are uploading to. Use QuickLook to preview the attachments to be uploaded. Join picture addresses easily and make comments for each individual file. Post article with addresses of your attachments easily within the app. Send Suggestions to the Author within RYGH mail system. Compress big images to certain size and quality.  title : The atvusb-creator Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The uber USB flash drive creator for the AppleTV. Creates USB flash drive based installers that include patchstick, factory restore and various LInux distributions. </p>

<p>Brought to you by the creators of atv-bootloader and many others. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>The Intel/PPC OSX version of  atvusb-creator.  </p>

<p>The Windows XP/Vista interim solution atv-win </p>

<p>Note that the current version is atvusb-creator-1.0.b13 and atv-win-3.0.zip </p>

<p> </p>

<p> </p>

<p>This version is comes with ssh, bin tools, and two plugins (XBMC/Boxee Installer/Launcher and SoftwareMenu). That&#39;s right, two full blown OSX applications with their own AppleTV plugin to launch AND get updates. And not only that but previous problems with launching an application into the front under all display resolutions has been resolved. </p>

<p>Remember that some USB flash drives just will not format correctly and if you have problems try another brand. Minimum flash size is 512MB. Follow the GUI and select &quot;ATV Patchstick&quot;, make sure to select the correct disk and hit the circling arrows to the left of the drive menu if you insert the USB flash drive after launching atvusb-creator. </p>

<p>The contents of the patchstick will look like the following, if yours does not look similar or is empty, then the creation failed and you need to create again either by pre-formating two hfsplus partitions using disk utility or trying a different brand flash drive. All USB flash drive are different, some work, some do not work. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>Standard patchstick rules: create the patchstick on your OSX box, power-down the AppleTV, insert the flash drive, power-up the AppleTV, wait for boot/patching, power-down again, remove flash drive and power up and enjoy XBMC for Mac (http://xbmc.org) or Boxee for Mac.(http://www.boxee.tv)  Remember that Boxee requires an account so if you don&#39;t have one, head on over to http://www.boxee.tv/atvusb and register for an account. </p>

<p>One final note (sure, sure), Both XBMC and Boxee are net installed from XBMC/Boxee launcher so remember to first select &quot;Update&quot; and install the individual applications. </p>

<p>Oh yes, atvusb-creator can be found in the downloads section so have at it and enjoy XBMC and Boxee native on the AppleTV OS. </p>

<p>The other two platform (Linux and Windows) will be released later.  </p>

<p>XBMC Launcher-0.8 has been released. Check the Update menu in either XBMC or Boxee Launchers. Not only can the Launcher update the Application but it can also update itself. Next for this version is the XBMC and Boxee Launchers have been combined into one. the launcher update will remove both of the older launchers and remove them with the new one. XBMC/Boxee Launcher issues should be goto http://code.google.com/p/atv-xbmc-launcher/issues/list  </p>

<p>Quick Help </p>

<p>1) if the sha1 checksum fails, then the download of the AppleTV update dmg failed and you need to delete it from the downloads folder. </p>

<p>2) WARNING DO NOT RUN atvusb-creator-1.0.0.b1 TWICE, there is an error that will require a AppleTV Factory Restore to fix if you run the PATCHSTICK twice. Much apologies if this has happened, do a factory restore and use b8. Once again, DO NOT RUN a patchstick made from atvusb-creator-1.0.0.b1.tar.gz TWICE.  UPDATE: This warning does not apply to versions greater than b1.  </p>

<p>3) And take the spaces out of the name of the folder name in atvusb-creator-1.0.b2.tar.gz </p>

<p>4) Users need to stop highjacking other issue threads. If you have a problem, please take the time to create an issue with a description of the problem. Otherwise I can&#39;t see that someone has added something different and respond and more important, others can find a previously solved issue with having to read every comment. </p>

<p>5) This uses the AppleTV update dmg and NOT the MacOSXUpdCombo10.4.9Intel.dmg or any other dmg. We are pulling out boot.efi from the AppleTV update dmg. Only this boot.efi will work for booting the AppleTV. The text above the &quot;Choose a DMG&quot; says &quot;Download AppleTV update DMG&quot; for a reason and no other DMG will work. </p>

<p>6) I&#39;m still seeing downloads of other version, the current version is atvusb-creator-1.0.b13 and this version does fix some issues that are present in the other versions. </p>

<p>7) WARNING Be very careful in selecting the correct USB device. Any USB mass storage devices are selectable and once you start the process, the contents are gone! A future version will have more info about the USB mass storage device selected and issue warning if the size is greater that 16GB. </p>

<p>8) If you are having problems under 10.5 getting the download to extract in Safari,  turn off auto expand in safari, then re-download and expand using the Finder. </p>

<p>Uninstall XBMC/BoxeeThis is done on the terminal after logging into the atv by ssh, but still pretty easy, as there are only a few folders to delete (password is frontrow): </p>

<p>login (if appletv.local does not work use the IP address of your AppleTV) </p>

<p>ssh frontrow@appletv.localdelete launcher and XBMC / Boxee </p>

<p>sudo rm -rf /Applications/{Boxee,XBMC}.app/ 
<br/>sudo rm -rf /System/Library/CoreServices/Finder.app/Contents/PlugIns/XBMCLauncher.frappliance/remove settings of Boxee and XBMC: </p>

<p>rm -rf /Users/frontrow/Library/Application\ Support/{BOXEE,XBMC}/reboot and that&#39;s it </p>

<p>sudo rebootmain</p>

 title : The audit-mass-assignment Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This SVN repository is no longer active!  The project has been MOVED to GitHub: </p>

<p>http://github.com/ryanlowe/audit_mass_assignment </p>

<p>The audit_mass_assignment Ruby on Rails plugin contains a rake task that checks the models in your project for the attr_accessible whitelist approach for protecting against &quot;mass assignment&quot; exploits.  It does not check for use of attr_protected! </p>

<p>If a Rails model does not use attr_accessible, it fails this audit.  The audit does not check which parameters are accessible or protected, only that at least one is marked as accessible. </p>

<p>You can run the audit periodically to make sure all of your project&#39;s models use attr_accessible.  Other audit plugins for Rails could be created to automatically check for bad patterns or insecure code.  This one was relatively easy. </p>

<p>./script/plugin install http://audit-mass-assignment.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/audit_mass_assignment/$ rake audit:mass_assignmentIf you want to protect ALL attributes use: </p>

<p>attr_accessible nilWhy are &quot;mass assignment&quot; exploits a danger to Rails applications?  See these links: </p>

<p>1. rorsecurity.info: Do not create records directly from form parameters </p>

<p>2. Railscasts: Hackers Love Mass Assignment </p>

<p>3. Rails Manual: Typical mistakes in Rails applications: Creating records directly from form parameters</p>

 title : The autoconnect Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The Auto Connect ProjectIntroductionThis module provides the handy ability to get a connection string from a client to server, without having to do specific configuration. The basic idea is the server broadcast on a small list of random ports. The client listens on one of these random ports. When it  receives the broadcast the data contains the connection string for the server.  </p>

<p>One example usage is in an internet cafe management system I developed. The client program was installed via a windows installer. Originally the user then had to edit the config for each machine in the shop. This was fine for one or two machines. However if you&#39;ve got 70+ machines this it took a long time to update the configuration. One solution is to have default set up locations. However if you have to move the server off the default or change it later, then you need to update all the clients again. </p>

<p>My solution to this was to use UDP broadcasts. The server ran a &#39;beacon&#39; when the clients &#39;watched&#39; for. When the client started it watched for the beacon. Upon &#39;seeing&#39; it, it was able to connect. The clients stopped watching for the server beacon until it lost its  connection or the server went down. This was very useful and was later expanded to tell  clients about other servers that were near by. </p>

<p>ExampleThe &quot;autoconnect.example&quot; contains an example client and server that models the basic idea. The &quot;test_server.py&quot; runs a simple XML-RPC server and the &quot;test_client.py&quot; discovers this and connects to call the greet() method. </p>

<p>The unit test case for this project also illustrate how the project is used. Look in the &quot;autoconnect.tests&quot; for further details.</p>

 title : The autofocus Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Autofocus is a Ruby on Rails web application that has been designed to allow users to organize themselves using the GTD philosophy.</p>
 summary : <p>AutoRest first public release 31/10/2007Simplify the development of rest based applications by using a generic controller implementation.  
<br/>Based on scaffold_resource of rails 1.2.3. 
<br/>   </p>

<p>With a single call of a class method, includes the default methods for a rest controller  
<br/>using user-supplied configuration. 
<br/>   Smart defaults are generated for all the missing configuration parameters. 
<br/>   </p>

<p>AuthorEmmanuel Oga. http://EmmanuelOga.WordPress.com 
<br/>UsageFor a complete sample app, check the sample app in the downloads. 
<br/>That app should be extracted to the root of the plugin. The sample app specs covers a great deal of the functionality that would be very difficult to spec without a complete rails app. 
<br/>By using the ar_spec_scaffold generator, a controller with all the options ready for customize is generated. 
<br/>   </p>

<p>The generator usage is the same as scaffold_resource: </p>

<p>ruby script/generate auto_rest ResourceName optional_field_1:type ... optional_field_n:type 
<br/>     </p>

<p>The optional fields are used only to include them on the migration. This generator produces also  
<br/>the proper specs on RAILS_ROOT/spec folder. You can use the --skip-rspecing to skip the generation 
<br/>of rspec-based specs. 
<br/>   Don&#39;t forget to: 
<br/>have rspec and rspec on rails plugins and have ran ruby script/generate rspec if you wish  to use rspec. 
<br/>      Set the routes. AutoRest is currently developed with a maximum 2-level  nesting of routes in mind. See http://weblog.jamisbuck.org/2007/2/5/nesting-resources 
<br/>        So it uses routes like 
<br/>         ActionController::Routing::Routes.draw do |map| 
<br/>search_opt= { :search =&gt; :get } 
<br/>         map.resources :zones, :collection =&gt; search_opt do |zone| 
<br/>zone.resources :customers, :name_prefix =&gt; &quot;zone&quot;  
<br/>end 
<br/>         map.resources :customers, :collection =&gt; search_opt 
<br/>end 
<br/>       For the integrated ferret support, you should put a :search =&gt; :get route on the collection of resources, just like i did above. Also include acts_as_ferret 
<br/>plugin and acts_as_ferret on the model class of the resource. 
<br/>       Set the proper resource relationships on models (has_many / belongs_to)      Create an application layout. If you include a call to ar_breadcrumbs in your layout, breadcrumbs will be available (i would say this is only usefull when you are working with nested resources).   &lt;!DOCTYPE HTML PUBLIC &quot;-//W3C//DTD HTML 4.01 Transitional//EN&quot; &quot;&lt;a href=&quot;http://www.w3.org/TR/html4/loose.dtd&quot;&gt;http://www.w3.org/TR/html4/loose.dtd&lt;/a&gt;&quot;&gt; AutoRest Test App  
<br/>  
<br/> 
<br/> 
<br/>           Configure each controller at your heart&#39;s content :)</p>
