 title : The avyenne Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Avyenneor living the &quot;not invented here&quot; syndrome </p>

<p>The purpose of this project is to learn to develop a text editor in Mono/.NET from scratch. </p>

<p>I really like the Emacs concept, but as you grow into elisp, you become too tied to it, at least in my opinion. Say &quot;reusability&quot;... I don&#39;t use elisp outside of Emacs and I&#39;ve heard some opinions on Emacs like &quot;lisp is not Haskell&quot; or similar. I&#39;ve been looking for an editor which supports just any extension/macro language I want to. </p>

<p>And I&#39;ve always wanted my own text editor (shoot me). ;) </p>

<p>So, what I&#39;d like to borrow from the Emacs concept is: </p>

<p>modes - I really like the concept of modes. I see them as extensible packages which define what I can do with a file. I&#39;d like them to feel more &quot;packaged&quot; but still abstract in terms of using common operations (like saving a file or &quot;M-x compile&quot;). transparent extensibility - Look up a function&#39;s description (C-h f in Emacs), get to the source file, modify it and use your modification without hitches, like restarting the editor. Eclipse, for example, annoys me when everytime I install a plugin it wants to be restarted. extensive documentation - Okay, I certainly will be lacking here for some time. :) But it should be there. integration with other tools - Show me the lines of source-code my compiler complains about. Call a debugger when I run into errors. configuration in the editor itself - I&#39;m not sure about that one. I really like the idea, but I still want to have the option to use some fancy dialogs. </p>

<p>What I&#39;d like to add: </p>

<p>script engines - Choose whatever you want, as far as there&#39;s a .Net implementation which creates assemblies. There are many already. Some of them are: IronPython, IronRuby, Boo, IronScheme (!!! well, in the perfect utopia of my mind, using IronScheme as extension language will in fact be some kind of &quot;package-oriented&quot; emacs) plugin concept - Everything besides the core should be a plugin. The plugin engine should not be vloated, like in Eclipse. I&#39;d like a straightforward solution. I&#39;ve tried mono-addins, but it just doesn&#39;t fit. I need to load assemblies directly (f.i. from script engines) refactoring - That is, keeping an AST in memory and using it. user interfaces as plugins - I don&#39;t want a definitive look. I want options for using the console, living in a Gnome environment, using the KDE look or MS Windows. Whatever there is or will be, I want to be able to put up a UI plugin which can handle the look of the user&#39;s environment. multithreading where it&#39;s useful - There are things which don&#39;t need to be synchronized that much. Like downloads of plugins for example? I want them to happen while I continue with what I was doing. Don&#39;t be too excessive here. Threads are evil in general. ;) </p>

<p>Problems: </p>

<p>I don&#39;t have any clue yet, how to embed a scripting language in .NET in an elegant way. I have a working boo scripting engine, but looking at the IronPython source, I&#39;m getting ashamed of myself. :) I don&#39;t know much about abstract syntax trees and how to use them. I know about ANTLR and how it builds parsers and lexers I could apparently use. I have some problems with the UI at the time. I began to create my own edit control but I noticed it took longer than I wished. So, I&#39;ll be switching to Scintilla or whatever and prepare an abstract layer. I know this will be as much work as an own editor. but I can implement the things as I need them and concentrate on the other features first. This project really needs a better name!</p>
 title : The awapi-local-db-sync Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The AdWords API Local Database Sync project is designed to simplify the process of maintaining a local store of AdWords account data. The scripts that make up the project can be used to schedule reports using the AdWords API, store the results in a local database (using SQLite), and then run queries against the database to determine, for instance, what AdWords account data has recently been added or updated. </p>

<p>The scripts are written in Python, and make use of the SOAPpy libraries for accessing the AdWords API SOAP service. The Python code is written against the dbapi2 database API, and by default it will use the SQLite implementation and store the report data in a SQLite database file on the local file system. It is possible to swap out the SQLite libraries for another database library that supports the dbapi2 interface.</p>

 title : The aws-todo Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Rails SimpleDB Task List (Implemented with Amazon Web Services)This project shows a simple implementation of a task list using the following technologies: </p>

<p>Ruby on Rails 2.02 Amazon SimpleDB Deployed on Amazon EC2 No local database is used. No MySQL or sqlite. </p>

<p>See the Setup for installation instructions. You will need an Amazon Web Services account. </p>

<p>This is a rather simple project, but I think it does a decent job in demonstrating the power of handing off infrastructure to third-party utility computing services (clouds) like EC2, S3, SQS, and SimpleDB. </p>

<p>It would be trivial to scale this application with a little bit of resource caching (calls to  Amazon) and an observer. You could deploy it on n servers (in fact there are scripts that will automatically drop in new EC2 instances based on CPU load) without any concerns over database clustering. Naturally you still need to develop with data integrity in mind, and ActiveResource has no where near the attention of ActiveRecord to date, so it&#39;s not a replacement for your typical relational DB setup in most instances. </p>

<p>Next Steps:Implement a proper caching layer at the controllers. Put a decent UI on it. Replace the proxy with direct calls to SimpleDB (we&#39;re marshalling objects twice right now). Put together the cap recipes for EC2 deployment. - Dave Rapin</p>

 title : The b2asm Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The B method is a rigorous software engineering process that is supported by a notation. The process starts with the creation of an initial model, composed essentially of state and operations. The state is a set of variables and an invariant condition that identifies the safe states. The operations may change the state of the model but shall be such that the invariant is preserved. Proof obligations that guarantee the overall consistency of the model are generated and must be discharged. The initial model is then the subject of successive refinements. Each refinement must also be checked rigorously. The result of the refinement process in the classic B method is an algorithmic level description of the operations that may then be synthesized to source code in a programming language. </p>

<p>The B method is supported by different industrial and academic tools. The purpose of this project is to provide techniques and tool support to extend the refinement process to generate assembly level description of the operations.</p>
 title : The babel-lang Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Babel is a language for talking with computers.  It is a knowledge representation language that aims to be as expressive as most natural language.  It is a formal grammar for representing thoughts and the meaning of human languages. </p>

<p>Babel is modeled after traditional computer programming languages that provide for terse, human readable and easy to write code.  </p>

<p>Parsing natural language is a hard problem, but it can be avoided by writing Babel.  By using this format natural language processing (NLP) can be separated from the real artificial intelligence work.  Babel provides a way to divide the two challenges. </p>

<p>Babel is not a representation of parsed natural language.  It is designed to represent specific meaning and does not include many of the subtleties of natural language.  Babel does not try to model natural language completely.  The aim is simply to be able to represent the meaning of most natural language.</p>

 title : The badges Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Badges is an authorization plugin (as in &quot;we don&#39;t need no stinking badges&quot; http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stinking_badges). </p>

<p>It does not provide authentication capability, nor it&#39;s own User model, but instead is meant to work with other authentication plugins such as acts_as_authenticated or restful_authentication.  You will need a User model, and the &#39;current_user&#39; method to be implemented at the controller level using an include. </p>

<p>Badges relies on the following domain model: A Privilege represents a particular named capability that is checked for authorization. Roles have a set of Privileges. Privileges can belong to more than one Role. Users can have one or more Roles. Users can have a role in general, or a role on an authorizable object, or on a Class of authorizable objects. </p>

<p>Badges enforces authorization by checking if a user has a particular privilege.  Users get privileges by having roles, as each role comes with a certain set of privileges.  Since what privileges a role has is stored in the database, it is easy to create new roles with different levels of privilege without needing to change any code, or to change existing roles while the application is running.  There is an included UI for updating roles and privileges. </p>

<p>Authorization can be checked at all layers of the application: view, controller, and model. </p>

<p>View: </p>

<p>  You have the privilege to  &#39;Are you sure?&#39;, :method =&gt; :delete %&gt; the project!</p>

<p>Controller: </p>

<p>  class FooController &lt; ApplicationController
<br/>  
<br/>    # need to have &#39;manage foos&#39; privilege to create, update or destroy
<br/>    privilege_required &#39;manage foos&#39;, :on=&gt;Some::Foo :only =&gt; [:create, :update, :destroy]
<br/>  endModel: </p>

<p>  class Project &lt; ActiveRecord::Base
<br/>    
<br/>    badges_authorizable_object</p>

<p>    privilege_required &#39;can create project&#39;=&gt;:create, &#39;can view projects&#39;=&gt;:find
<br/>        
<br/>  end</p>

<p>Barcode Generator for Rails - ReDuxBarcode generator makes generating/displaying barcodes in any format like, PNG,JPEG,JPG etc.. for any alphanumeric id, a piece of cake. </p>

<p>It uses Gbarcode for encoding barcode data and ImageMagick to generate  images out of it for displaying in views.(yes yes.. you read it correct, its NOT using RMagick anymore) </p>

<p>This way we can generate any barcode type which Gbarcode -&gt; Gnome Barcode project supports. </p>

<p>USAGEits as simple as saying  </p>

<p> This will generate a barcode for FJJ4JD in BARCODE_39 format with default width and height and include it in the view. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>the images are stored in /public/images/barcodes subdir. </p>

<p>Options Options Options ..to customize your barcodes, you can optionally pass following information in your views  </p>

<p>encoding_format (Gbarcode constants for eg. Gbarcode::BARCODE_128 etc..) width height scaling_factor xoff yoff margin   in this case your view will look like : </p>

<p> 100, 
<br/>                    :width  =&gt; 400,
<br/>		    :margin =&gt; 100,
<br/>		    :xoff   =&gt; 20,
<br/>		    :yoff   =&gt; 40
<br/>%&gt; this will produce something beautiful like this .... </p>

<p> </p>

 title : The basecampjs Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This is a JavaScript wrapper for the Basecamp API. It covers everything in the API except file attachments for comments and messages. For the API to work it has to be used in an environment like AIR where cross-domain XMLHttpRequest calls are allowed. </p>

<p>Here is an example of getting back an Array of projects from Basecamp. </p>

<p>var basecamp = new Basecamp(&quot;your.basecamp.url&quot;, &quot;user_name&quot;, &quot;password&quot;);
<br/>basecamp.projects({
<br/>	success: function( projects_xml ) {
<br/>		var projects = Basecamp.Project.from_xml( projects_xml );
<br/>		alert( projects.length );
<br/>	}
<br/>};Here is an example of how to create a new message assuming you&#39;ve already used the API to retrieve the desired project_id, message_category_id and person_id. </p>

<p>var message = new Basecamp.Message({
<br/>	title: &quot;Testing from API&quot;,
<br/>	body: &quot;This is a test from the JavaScript API wrapper.&quot;,
<br/>	category_id: message_category_id
<br/>});
<br/>basecamp.post_message( project_id, message, [person_id], {
<br/>	success: function( message_xml ) {
<br/>		var message = Basecamp.Message.from_xml( message_xml )[0];
<br/>		alert( message.id );
<br/>	}
<br/>});Why?I finally found some time to explore Adobe AIR and thought ... &quot;Hey, why don&#39;t I write an AIR app for Basecamp.&quot; The first step was to write this API wrapper/adapter so that I could easily communicate with Basecamp. </p>

<p>RoadmapIf I continue to find time (and have a Basecamp account to play with) this API will surely evolve as I begin to use the different parts while building the AIR app. Beware that as it stands right now this API wrapper is mostly untested. </p>

<p>I&#39;m particularly anxious to add the file uploading for messages and comments. </p>

<p>DocumentationFirst place to look is the actual Basecamp API documentation (http://developer.37signals.com/basecamp/index.shtml). Currently this API follows their Ruby wrapper (http://developer.37signals.com/basecamp/basecamp.rb) very closely. Other than that ... its all code for now. :)</p>

 title : The baseutils Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Homepage: http://www.fvue.nl/wiki/Bash_completion_library </p>

<p>This project splits the bash completion package of Ian Macdonald (see: http://www.caliban.org/bash/index.shtml#completion) into multiple files. </p>

<p>The objectives of this project are that bash completion: </p>

<p>should load faster should consume less memory should have an open development environment should have automated tests </p>

<p>Should load fasterBash-completion-lib loads 10 times faster as does the single file bash completion package. </p>

<p>Should consume less memoryCompletion functions are loaded run-time for only those commands you actually complete - the moment you press TAB.  After the first completion, the completion function is installed and stays in memory for fast subsequent completions. </p>

<p>Should have an open development environmenthttp://code.google.com/p/bash-completion-lib/ </p>

<p>Should have automated testsDejaGnu is used to run automated tests. </p>

<p>Roadmap                      GOALS                                         REALISATION
<br/>     ------------------------------------------   -----------------------------------------------
<br/>(1)  Improve bash-completion-20060301:            bash_completion_lib-1.3.1:
<br/> |   - improve initial loading speed              - loads 10x faster
<br/> |   - improve completions                        - contains fixes of 20060301-debian4
<br/> |                                                - contains fixes of 20060301-ubuntu1
<br/> |   - split completions into separate files      - split into 543 files for 609 completions
<br/> |   - add testsuite                              - contains a DejaGnu testsuite with &gt; 1200 tests
<br/> |
<br/> |
<br/>(2)  Patch bash, so that real dynamic loading     - bash-4.0 contains a `compopt&#39; builtin
<br/> |   becomes possible:                            - Fedora has patched bash-3 with a catch-all
<br/> |   - add `complete-not-found&#39; handler to bash     programmable completion handler
<br/> |   - add `compset&#39; bash builtin
<br/> |
<br/> |
<br/>(3)  Improve bash-completion to do real           --
<br/>     dynamic loading</p>
 title : The bash-completion-lib Open Source Project on Open Hub
 title : The bashstyle-ng Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>BashStyle-NGIntroductionBashStyle-NG is a graphical Tool for changing the Bash’s behaviour and look’n&#39;feel. Aswell as Readline’s, Nano’s and Vim’s. </p>

<p>It shipps a huge scriptchain, that is used by the styles shipped with BS-NG, but can also be used separately. Since v6.3 you have the opportunity to create your own prompts. For important notes on how to do so, refer back to the documentation. </p>

<p>If you don’t understand an option or something does not work as expected read the documentation. It’s installed in /usr/share/doc/bashstyle-ng/index.html ( /usr is default but may vary if you passed an other prefix to configure). </p>

<p>Currently BS-NG shipps 15 pre-defined Styles for your prompt. Most of them can be modified via the Custom Prompt Builder. If you want to save your current configuration and want to re-import it later (or for using it on a different user/machine) you can do so via the Profiler (bs-ng-profiler --help). </p>

<p>Standalone (GConf-Free) Configuration (for faster Bash-Startup) can be created via the RCGenerator (rcgenerator --help). </p>

<p>SVN AccessYou can get the latest in-development version by running: </p>

<p>svn co http://bashstyle-ng.googlecode.com/svn/trunk bashstyle-ng </p>

<p>Once you’ve done the initial checkout you can use svn up to update the svn. </p>

<p>Use svn log to see the full set of changes or svn log –limit (number of log messages) for a limited number of entries </p>

<p>TranslationsCurrent Translations:de (German): 99% (Christopher Roy Bratusek)  it (Italian): 99% (Alin Hantig) </p>

<p>Work-In-Progress Translations:ru (Russian): 0% (Alex Lushpai) / 99% in SVN </p>

<p>New TranslationsIf you want to translate BashStyle-NG into another language than above (or want to update one of the above translations) then do it, and send me the po file via mail. </p>

<p>If you don&#39;t know how to do so, don&#39;t be shy and simply ask me for instructions. </p>

<p>IdeasIf you got an Feature Request or a new Idea for BashStyle-NG, then don&#39;t hesitate to post it! If you can provide patches, then that&#39;s even better :) </p>

<p>BugsReport Bugs either via mail, on my blog or via the Issues page right here. </p>

<p>Before reporting bugs you make sure that you got the latest version of bashstyle-ng (svn) </p>

<p>InstallationDebian &amp; Cosimply download the debian package and do: </p>

<p>dpkg -i  </p>

<p>Any other Distro./configure make sudo make install (or: su -c &quot;make install&quot;) </p>

<p>Have Fun!</p>

 title : The batched-sql-fu Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>BatchedSqlFuThis is vendor specific to MySQL or any RDBMS that supports the syntax : </p>

<p>INSERT INTO </p>

<p>(col1, col2) VALUES (&#39;val1&#39;, &#39;val2&#39;), (&#39;val3&#39;, &#39;val4&#39;), (&#39;val5&#39;, &#39;val6&#39;). </p>

<p>What it does is it overrides the insert method of the connection adapter for the duration of the block and flushes inserts every after 100 inserts are by the value you specify. </p>

<p>ExampleLine.insert_by_batch do </p>

<p>Line.create(:text =&gt; &#39;Hello&#39;) 
<br/>Line.create(:text =&gt; &#39;World&#39;) 
<br/>end </p>

<p>all statements will be the executed in one SQL. </p>

<p>Installruby script/plugin install http://batched-sql-fu.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/batched_sql_fu </p>

<p>CaveatsYou might not receive the expected result from Line.create or Line.save  since the statements are executed later. </p>

<p>This plugin is experimental. Use it at your own risk! </p>

<p>Copyright (c) 2008 David, released under the MIT license</p>

<p>   </p>

<p>More about the projectThe project name, swarm, is a suggestion about its core value: the ability to extract a global quantitative meaning from apprently meaningless elements (such as single words), just in the same way a swarm behaves in a coherent way even if the behaviour of the single insect is erratic.  Learn more about Bayes-Swarm in the GetStarted page. </p>

 title : The bayesian-inference Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This package is a collection of useful classes for basic Bayesian inference. Currently, its main goal is to be a tool for learning and exploration of Bayesian probabilistic calculations.  </p>

<p>Currently it also includes subpackages for stochastic simulation tools which are not strictly related to Bayesian inference, but are currently being developed within BIP. One such package is the BIP.SDE which contains a parallelized solver for stochastic differential equations, an implementation of the Gillespie direct algorithm. </p>

<p>The Subpackage Bayes also offers a tool for parameter estimation of Deterministic and Stochastic Dynamical Models. This tool will be fully described briefly in a scientific paper currently submitted for publication.  </p>

<p>I hope that in time it will mature into an useful tool for general use.</p>

 summary : <p>09/07/2007 by Krzysztof G. </p>

<p>TODO List: </p>

<p>Add list of all the files inside the backup directory, which will be easily searchable, list in the form of text file will be included in root of the 
<br/>backup directory. 
<br/>Add script to automate the whole process (including burning the CD/DVD) using anacron/cron functionality. 
<br/>Add notification capability which informs the user of scanning performed and alerts when the backup exceeds preferred value in MB. 
<br/>Possibly more to come... </p>

<p>09/07/2007 by Krzysztof G. </p>

<p>Simple backup utility written in Ruby programming language! This project consists of just a small bunch of scripts, mainly to deal with XML configuration files. </p>

<p>Features: 
<br/>As you are probably aware at this point, this is a console based application Gathers files from many locations Keeps track of the data and copy only new files or the ones with different timestamps Keeps track of the previous backups to prevent storing the same files on different CD&#39;s Is configurable with simple wizard Has logging facility Checks the size of the backup folder and notify the user when it exceeds preferred size Checks the size of the file before adding it to the backup folder to see if it fits More or less that&#39;s all. Well, there are a few things someone who wants to try it should know. First, there is not much validation in place so please enter the data as specified in the examples when running the configuration utility. Second, the source is not commented in a very sophisticated way, but I think everyone who wants to tweak it a bit will find out what is where. The utility has no name yet, so feel free to send me some if you find this tool useful at all. The whole application consists of two main scripts, one for running configuration program and the other for running actual backup. </p>

<p>Installation: </p>

<p>This utility was written for Linux and for Linux only! Tested on Ubuntu 7.04. You would have to have ruby installed, check www.ruby-lang.org for download and installation instructions. For the application itself just download the tar.gz folder from the link below, unpack it, and you&#39;re ready to go! </p>

<p>Setup: </p>

<p>Simply run backupConfig.rb file (you can make it executable with chmod or run ruby filename.rb) and follow the rabbit. </p>

<p>Run: </p>

<p>Run bckp.rb similarly to backupConfig.rb, if you have ruby in place just make sure you have an -x flag set on this file or run ruby bckp.rb and you are ready to go. Before running bckp you have to run config utility to have all the settings in place. </p>

<p>If anyone will find it interesting, wants to learn some Ruby and would like to extend its functionality let me know and I put the files somewhere in cvs or subversion server. Possible enhancements include: </p>

<p>GUI with GTK2 or some other Linux aware toolkit some kind of notification facilities launching external CD/DVD burner or similar functionality If someone has some more ideas please feel free and let me know. </p>

<p>This script was written on Netbeans 6.0 M9 development version with Ruby support. </p>

<p>Download: </p>

<p># Non-members may check out a read-only working copy anonymously over HTTP. svn checkout http://bckp.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ bckp </p>

<p>For NetBeans check out, you can follow my tutorial posted earlier on this blog! </p>

<p>This is my first program in Ruby which is more complicated than famous &#39;hello world&#39; so don&#39;t expect anything astonishing.</p>

 title : The bcmsscaffoldresource Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>BComposer - Bulletin composition made easierIntroductionCreated to handle a complete mailout bulletin system, providing powerful features for administrators including user access and project based restrictions, and a simple live-editing interface for non-technical users. </p>

<p>A template system is provided using Liquid templates so that designers and programmers can create complex bulletins. which can be later &quot;filled-in&quot; my non-technical people, and not have to worry about a WYSIWYG editor causing havoc to the designs. </p>

<p>Recipients are managed on a per project-group basis, which means they can be shared between projects in the same group. This is a powerful feature that allows projects to share the same code base. </p>

<p>The project is currently of alpha quality. Although it will work perfectly well in most situations, there are still a few important features missing which may limit its implementation value. </p>

<p>Project DocumentationThis is still a big work in progress, so please expect more details soon. </p>

<p>Currently, BComposer is only recommend for experienced users as much of its functionality is not yet documented.  </p>

<p>InstalationInstructions - Basic instructions on how to get started and some requirements. FeatureRequests - some of the features that aren&#39;t quite there yet or are planned. CreatingTemplates - methods available for use in your Liquid base templates. ScreenShots - coming soon ... ProjectsUsingBcomposer - some (public) mailing lists which are using the application. InternationalisationGettext is supported although not fully implemented throughout the project. Currently Spanish and English are supported, but more can be added easily. If you would like to see BComposer in another language, please download the gettext source pot file, and create a new translation using a program like poEdit. </p>

<p>Who made this?This project was created by Sam Lown to initially provide a simple bulletin list program for the company Internet21 in Madrid. More interest came about for the project from other contacts and the project was subsequently released as Open Source. </p>

<p>If you find this program useful, I&#39;d love to hear from you, especially if you have made any modifications that could be back-ported to the main trunk. </p>

<p>Currently, I&#39;m quite busy on other projects, but should you wish for any further functionality and don&#39;t have the programming support in house, please get in contact with me. </p>

<p>LicenseThis project is licensed under the GNU General Public License v3. You are free to use this application as you see fit, with the restriction that any changes you make and subsequently distribute, must be publicly available. </p>

<p>After some thought, the Affero GPL license has not been used, subsequently you are free to modify the code for private use and provide a public service based on your code. Of course, any resale or distribution must include the source, and no fees can be made for the code itself. I would of course very much like to hear from anyone interested in creating a public service based on the project for support or features, and accept donations. </p>

<p>A dual-license may also be considered as currently I am the only author of the project, although I may take some convincing. Of course, any publicly contributed code could not be included without the explicit permission of the contributor. Contracted modifications for private use are however acceptable provided the code is not later distributed. </p>

<p>These comments are based on the information provided by the GNU, in relation to this project.</p>

 title : The bear-project Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>BEARはページ&amp;リソース指向でイベント駆動型のDI PHPアプリケーションフレームワークです。 </p>

<p>ページ </p>

<p>&lt;?php</p>

<p>require &#39;App.php&#39;;</p>

<p>/**
<br/> * 記事一覧表示ページ
<br/> *
<br/> * @package Page
<br/> * @author  $Author:$
<br/> * @version SVN: Release: $Id: $
<br/> */
<br/>class Page_User_Entry extends App_Page
<br/>{</p>

<p>    /**
<br/>     * インジェクト
<br/>     *
<br/>     */
<br/>    public function onInject()
<br/>    {
<br/>        $this-&gt;_resource = BEAR::dependency(&#39;BEAR_Resource&#39;);
<br/>        $this-&gt;injectGet(&#39;id&#39;);
<br/>    }</p>

<p>    /**
<br/>     * 初期化
<br/>     *
<br/>     * @requied id
<br/>     */
<br/>    public function onInit(array $args)
<br/>    {
<br/>        $params = array(&#39;uri&#39; =&gt; &#39;User&#39;, &#39;values&#39; =&gt; $args);
<br/>        $this-&gt;_resource-&gt;read($params)-&gt;link(&#39;entry&#39;)-&gt;set();
<br/>    }</p>

<p>    /**
<br/>     * 出力
<br/>     *
<br/>     */
<br/>    public function onOutput()
<br/>    {
<br/>        $this-&gt;display();
<br/>    }
<br/>}
<br/>$options = array(&#39;cache&#39; =&gt; array(&#39;type&#39; =&gt; &#39;init&#39;, &#39;life&#39; =&gt; 10));
<br/>App_Main::run(&#39;Page_User_Entry&#39;, $options);リソース </p>

<p>&lt;?php
<br/>/**
<br/> * エントリーリソース
<br/> *
<br/> */
<br/>class App_Ro_Entry extends App_Ro
<br/>{
<br/>    /**
<br/>     * インジェクト
<br/>     */
<br/>    public function onInject()
<br/>    {
<br/>        parent::onInject();
<br/>        $this-&gt;_queryConfig[&#39;pager&#39;] = 1;  // DBページャー利用
<br/>        $this-&gt;_queryConfig[&#39;perPage&#39;] = 5; //画面毎のアイテム数
<br/>        $this-&gt;_queryConfig[&#39;deleted_at&#39;] = true; //論理削除対応
<br/>        $this-&gt;_queryConfig[&#39;sort&#39;] = array(array(&#39;created&#39;, &#39;date&#39;, &#39;+&#39;)); //ソートクエリー可
<br/>        $this-&gt;_query = BEAR::dependency(&#39;BEAR_Query&#39;, $this-&gt;_queryConfig, false);
<br/>    }</p>

<p>    /**
<br/>     * リソース作成　(AOPトランザクション)
<br/>     *
<br/>     * @required user_id
<br/>     * @required body
<br/>     *
<br/>     * @aspect App_Aspect_Transaction
<br/>     */
<br/>    public function onCreate($values)
<br/>    {
<br/>        $values[&#39;created_at&#39;] = _BEAR_DATETIME; //現在時刻
<br/>        $result = $this-&gt;_query-&gt;insert($values);
<br/>        if ($this-&gt;_query-&gt;isError($result)) {
<br/>            throw $this-&gt;_exception(&#39;登録できませんでした&#39;, 500);
<br/>        }
<br/>    }</p>

<p>    /**
<br/>     * リソース読み込み
<br/>     *
<br/>     * ソートとDBページャーとRow/All取得に対応します
<br/>     */
<br/>    public function onRead($values)
<br/>    {
<br/>        $sql = &quot;SELECT * FROM entries&quot;;
<br/>        $result = $this-&gt;_query-&gt;select($sql, array(), $values);
<br/>        return $result;
<br/>    }
<br/>}テンプレート </p>

 title : The beast-mcmc Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>BEAST, Bayesian Evolutionary Analysis Sampling Trees, is a cross-platform program for Bayesian MCMC analysis of molecular sequences. It is orientated towards (strict and relaxed) molecular clock analyses. It can be used as a method of constructing phylogenies, but it is also intended for testing evolutionary hypotheses without conditioning on a single tree topology. BEAST uses MCMC to average over tree space, so that each tree is weighted proportional to its posterior probability. It uses an XML input format that allows the user to design and run a large range of models. We also include a program that can convert NEXUS files into this format. </p>

<p>What can BEAST do? </p>

 title : The beerbottle Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Project Beer Bottle is a hard drive encryption scheme designed to allow flexible use of a computer while protecting all sensitive information. </p>

<p>By overlaying an unencrypted base install with an encrypted filesystem via UnionFS, all changes made to a system are unreadable to an unauthorized user. This would include not only valuable personal or proprietary information, but any other data which may seem harmless, but as an aggregate provide more information about the users than they would like available to a thief or anybody else who might acquire physical access. </p>

<p>There exists the option for a duress password which would cause the encrypted partition to be overwritten seamlessly, presenting what appears to be a fresh install to the intruder. </p>

<p>At the moment, we do not have any scripts written. If you check the source tree, we do have fairly detailed instructions. We would be glad of any comments you might have.</p>

 title : The benchmarkforrails Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>BenchmarkForRails addresses a few blind spots in Rails&#39; benchmarking: </p>

<p>query construction costs before/after filters session management </p>

<p>See How Rails&#39; Benchmarks Lie for more about the blind spots in Rails&#39; benchmarks. </p>

<p>Other strengths: </p>

<p>BenchmarkForRails.watch makes it very easy to benchmark new methods without implementing your own alias_method_chain automatically handles methods called multiple times (e.g. ActiveRecord::Base#find) </p>

<p>Installation: </p>

<p>Install the plugin from SVN (http://benchmarkforrails.googlecode.com/svn/trunk) however you normally would (piston, script/plugin install, etc.) and you&#39;re done. If you want to add benchmarks, look at the plugin&#39;s init.rb for easy examples.</p>

 title : The berkeleyaligner Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The BerkeleyAligner is a word alignment software package that implements recent innovations in unsupervised word alignment.  To learn more about the project and surrounding research, visit the Berkeley word aligner website. </p>

<p>News9/28 As of release 2.1, we have split the Berkeley aligner into two downloads.  The unsupervised aligner doesn&#39;t require a set of hand-labeled word alignments.  The supervised aligner does, and it depends on the unsupervised aligner. </p>

<p>Recent changes and bug fixes9/28 You can now run the unsupervised aligner without a hand-aligned test set; the evaluation phase will be skipped. </p>

<p>9/28 Loading trained models for evaluation only now works correctly (just give an empty training sequence) </p>

<p>9/28 Output can now be split into multiple alignment files corresponding to multiple input files (alignInputsSeparately option) </p>

<p>9/28 The test set does not need to be included in the training sets</p>

 title : The beziercurve Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Lets you create and on the fly edit bezier curves with an easy syntax. You can add as many anchor and control points as you want. </p>

<p>How to useimport beziercurve.BezierCurve;
<br/>import beziercurve.display.AnchorPoint;
<br/>import beziercurve.display.ControlPoint;
<br/>import beziercurves.events.BezierEvent;</p>

<p>...</p>

<p>BezierCurve.verbose = true;</p>

<p>var b:BezierCurve = new BezierCurve(0, 0xFF0000, 1);
<br/>addChild(b);</p>

<p>b.addAnchor(x, y);
<br/>b.addControl(x, y);
<br/>b.addAnchor(x, y);
<br/>b.addControl(x, y);
<br/>b.addControl(x, y);
<br/>b.addControl(x, y);
<br/>b.addAnchor(x, y);
<br/>b.addAnchor(x, y);</p>

<p>var a0:AnchorPoint = new AnchorPoint(x, y);
<br/>var a1:AnchorPoint = new AnchorPoint(x, y);
<br/>var c0:ControlPoint = new ControlPoint(x, y);
<br/>b.addPath(a0, c0, a1);</p>

<p>b.editable = true;
<br/>b.showEditor = true;</p>

<p>b.addEventListener(BezierEvent.START_EDITING, startEditCurve);
<br/>b.addEventListener(BezierEvent.END_EDITING, endEditCurve);Documentationonline http://www.nicolaslevavasseur.com/beziercurves/ or download here</p>

Apple gave us that spiffy new HUD window but no controls to put on it.  So I started my own.  Yes I know there are a few good AppKits out there already to achive the desired look, but they use images to create the components.  I have hand drawn every one of these controls using ONLY native Cocoa drawing functions (NSBezierPath, NSGradient, etc...)  This makes them resolution independant and makes your app less heavy come distribution time</p>

<p>This project aims to follow the principles of least surprise, human factor and simplicity of use. </p>

<p>DownloadsWindows users can download the file at the Download Page and just run the installer. </p>

<p>Other operating systems users should download the source file from the Download Page, install the dependencies (Ruby, Ruby-GNOME2 and SQLite3-Ruby) and then run: </p>

<p># ruby install.rb </p>

<p>Debian user should download specific file from the Download Page and install it with: </p>

<p># dpkg -i bibliomori_XXX_all.deb </p>

 title : The bicycleledpov Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Image (C) www.ladyada.net </p>

<p>See the last activity on the project: </p>

<p>read the development news; watch the recent changes on SVN;  see the last messages on discussion group. </p>

<p>IntroductionBicycle LED POV is an electronic LED bar to attach on bicycle wheels. When riding the bicycle, the LED bar will draw with light, text messages and image animations. </p>

<p>Custom text messages and animations will be drawn on a PC software and downloaded using an USB cable. </p>

<p>Goals of the projectcreate a Free/Open hardware, firmware and software LED POV for bicycle wheels; easy to use for non electronics technician people; find some company that wants to sell PCBs, kits or final assembled product;   use only Free Software tools as possible, like CAD software for PCB design, C compiler for MCU firmware, etc; open to improvements and new ideas from community. Your participationBecause hacking is fun and projects are like life, always evolving, If you have any ideas, If you think you can improve the project, If you want to say something, please leave a message on the discussion group. This project is a work in progress, It&#39;s an effort to improve actual bicycle LED POVs as the SpokePOV from Ladyada. There is room for a lot of improvements as the project involves different areas as: </p>

<p>mechanics; electronics; software; LED art; animations; demos. </p>

<p>DescriptionBicycle LED POV is an electronic LED bar to attach on bicycle wheels. A magnet is also attached on a fixed part of the bicycle (as example, the fork), so the hall effect sensor mounted on the Bicycle LED POV can detect each full rotation of the wheel. </p>

<p>Bicycle LED POV consist of mainly three different parts: Hardware; Software and Firmware. </p>

<p>Hardware </p>

<p>HaRdware consist of an electronics printed circuit board with LEDs and a few components as a microcontroller unit, a memory to hold the text messages and image animations, an USB connector and 2 NiMh cells. </p>

<p>See more information on HaRdware page &gt;&gt; </p>

<p>FirmwareFiRmware is the software that will be inside the MCU, it will configure the hardware system to work as needed. </p>

<p>See more information on FiRmware page &gt;&gt; </p>

<p>SoftwareSoFtware is a PC Free Software program to send text messages and image animations to the HaRdware. </p>

<p>See more information on SoFtware page &gt;&gt;</p>
 summary : <p>Bifbotka is an Active Scaffold Ruby on Rails web application that takes a file, extracts transactions, allows user to modify transactions and then outputs Agresso Business World friendly file such as BIF or Excel CSV file. </p>

<p>It is based on the highly successful Propmansheet web application. </p>

<p>This example is used to post Housing Benfit Refund Cheques.  Modify and make new applications to post different types of items. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>TO SET-UP (once only) </p>

<p>To install download and install instant rails (http://instantrails.rubyforge.org/wiki/wiki.pl). </p>

<p>Extract latest bifbotka zip (get from Downloads) to rails_app directory. </p>

<p>Open rails console window. </p>

<p>Set-up database: </p>

<p>mysqladmin -u root create bifbotka_development </p>

<p>rake db:migrate </p>

<p>TO RUN </p>

<p>Run rails: </p>

<p>ruby script/server </p>

<p>Go to website: </p>

<p>http://localhost:3000/bifinfo </p>

<p>Use webpage to input file and output BIF++ </p>

<p>contact ezzy@digiworld.com for queries </p>

<p>( ++ based on Batch_input_file_format_55 and IBS interfaces doc Export creditor file CO-CRED-INTERFACE)</p>

 title : The bifbotkasql Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Bifbotka SQL is an Active Scaffold Ruby on Rails web application that uses a SQL query, extracts transactions from Agresso then allows user to modify transactions and then outputs s friendly file such as a tab delimited text or Excel CSV file.  </p>

<p>It is based on the highly successful Propmansheet web application and original bifBOTka application.  </p>

<p>This example is used to post cash payments from the Agresso bank statement to the IBS Revenue and Benefits System.  </p>

<p>You can use this code as a basis to make new applications to post different types of items. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>[ </p>

<p>screen print of original bifbotka </p>

<p>TO SET-UP (once only) </p>

<p>To install download and install instant rails (http://instantrails.rubyforge.org/wiki/wiki.pl). </p>

<p>Extract latest bifbotkasql zip (get from Downloads) to rails_app directory. </p>

<p>copy access details to Agresso database to by copying emailed &quot;database.yml&quot; to C:\InstantRails\rails_apps\bifbotkaSQL\config directory. </p>

<p>Open rails console window. </p>

<p>Change directory to bifbotkasql: </p>

<p>cd bifbotkasql </p>

<p>Set-up database: </p>

<p>mysqladmin -u root create bifbotkasql_development </p>

<p>rake db:migrate </p>

<p>TO RUN </p>

<p>Run rails: </p>

<p>ruby script/server </p>

<p>Go to website: </p>

<p>http://localhost:3000/sqlbifinfo </p>

<p>Use webpage to connect to Agresso and output tab delimited IBS file++ </p>

<p>contact ezzy@digiworld.com for queries </p>

 title : The bio-vet Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This is a somewhat random collection of bioinformatics programs and libraries written in Java/Groovy.   Or it will be, once I get a chance to prepare and upload some of the things I&#39;ve written.   </p>

<p>Note: This project is distinct and separate from the BioGroovy project which is built on top of BioJava.   I support the  BioGroovy/BioJava projects and don&#39;t want to cause any confusion, so when I get a chance to figure out how, I will change the name of my Google code project.  </p>

<p>AboutRecently I have found Groovy and Java together to be a very productive agile tool set.  For me, almost all development starts with a simple script that generates some smallish analysis that I have to do before the end of the day.  Over time, I end up reusing this code and improving it and often I end up having to build large-scale pipelines to do these same analysis in bulk.    Goovy+Java gives me a very smooth path to do this </p>

<p> Write quick and dirty single file scripts in Groovy to get today&#39;s results out.   If those prove useful, abstract the core bits out into reusable Groovy classes.   If those prove useful repeatedly invest the minimal effort to translate into Java.   Since Groovy can mix in Java classes with zero impedance, I am able to tap into the entire rich world of Java libraries in my quick-and-dirty one off scripts.   Moreover, since these libraries are distributed as JAR files compiled for the JVM, I can be almost certain that if I see a library somewhere on the web I want to use that I can download it, drop it in my groovy lib directory,  and it will just work.   This contrasts with languages where there is frequently some native component to compile, introducing a huge uncertainty as to whether or not I will be able to get a particular library to even install for me today, much less get the analysis results I need out and to my many customers.   In my field, it&#39;s all about getting results today, while somehow building an infrastructure for the long term in the background virtually for free.   Groovy/Java lets me do this.    </p>

<p>Without Groovy, Java is a poor choice for an agile bioinformatics language.  The syntax is noisy and employs maximal bondage (must tediously throw or catch all exceptions, etc.).  Those are good features for large projects, but when your project is in the early &quot;results today!!&quot; mode, it&#39;s not acceptable.   Moreover, java itself has clunky invocation syntax that usually forces you to wrap it in a shell script just to hide the ugliness from the user.    Groovy solves almost all of the issues that Java has an agile language.    Groovy can be run as a script or compiled, has lazy typing with dynamic type resolution, lots of syntatic sugar, Perl/Ruby-like regular expression syntax, list and hash syntax, easy deployment, etc.    </p>

<p>Obtain Groovy and read more about it here: </p>

<p>http://groovy.codehaus.org/</p>

 title : The biohacker Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Mistakes are the portals of discovery. James Joyce (1882-1941) </p>

<p>A metabolic network is defined as the set of biochemical reactions that the enzymes coded for in an organism&#39;s genome are capable of catalyzing. When the network of an organism is derived from pathway databases, it needs to be debugged for </p>

<p>incoherences e.g., the metabolic model must obey mass balance laws. 
<br/>incompleteness e.g., the metabolic model is missing known reactions, genes, or compounds 
<br/>inconsistencies e.g., the metabolic model is inconsistent with experimental results 
<br/>Because of these issues, reconstructing metabolic networks from annotated genomes is currently a time-consuming, error-prone process. </p>

<p>We develop BioHacker, a debugger for metabolic networks. BioHacker not only detects these issues, but also generates explanations as to where the problems lie and generates hypotheses for how to fix them. </p>

<p>Read the BioHacker paper (PDF). Check out the source code.</p>

 summary : <p>The aim of this project is to provide an alternate method of providing traditional CAPTCHAs (http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captcha). CAPTCHA are devices that provide web forums and other web based resources with protection from computer generated spam.  Current techniques for the creation of CAPTCHAs are not compatible with the tools,  necessary for users with visual impairments to effectively use resources protected by CAPTCHAs.  Traditional CAPTCHAs are designed to prevent optical character recognition tools(OCR) thus tools for the visually impaired are not able to interpret the contents of the CAPTCHA.  Current methods of providing CAPTCHAs for the visually impaired use audio versions of the CAPTCHA, this version is susceptible to speach recognition software and as such distorted sounds are added to defeat this type of attack.  However this method is not ideal in noisy environments such as Coffee shops and offices where it can be challenging to distinguish between the environments background nose, distortions which are used to defeat speech recognition software and the contents of the CAPTCHA.  This results in numerous erroneous inputs and a frustrated user. </p>

<p>The method we propose requires the user to classify images correctly, in-order to verify that they are not an automated spamming program.   An example of this process would be for the user to be displayed five images: the sun, a person jumping, Batman, a flower and a pizza.  The user will be asked to select the images which describe action, as jumping is an action and Batman is an action film, then these two images would be the correct answer. This method can not be replicated by a computer program, making the complex associations between images and words which is currently not within the capabilities of computers and will remain so for the foreseeable future. </p>

<p>Project Objectives: </p>

<p>  The creation of technology for the collection of large numbers of images to be used with the CAPTCHA system. </p>

<p>  To develop the machinery for the categorising of large numbers of images, through the use of human volunteers. </p>

<p>  To create a prototype using the categorised images. </p>

<p>  Conduct usability testing with the aide of target users. </p>

<p>  To report the findings in a written report, appropriate for publication or dissemination.</p>

 summary : <p>GoalsUse Boehm GC library for memory management Make C core as small as possible Write as much code in the Lisp dialect itself (make it largely self-hosting, like Glasgow Haskell) Use the pair/list data structure(s) whenever possible as the data structure(s) (taking a cue from Lua - which did, in turn, from Scheme) Incorporate influences from &quot;pure&quot; functional programming languages like Haskell Consistent error-handling at C and Lisp levels For now, a very forgiving dynamic type system InfluencesHaskell Lua Arc All the Lisps and Schemes, of course Python because it&#39;s my favorite language and so bound to creep in somewhere AboutThe writer is a university student interested in compilers and interpreters.  title : The blisscarot Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Chaque machine supervisée du parc a un « agent » déployé dessus, qui tourne en arrière-plan. Il s&#39;agit d&#39;un script Ruby que je vous fournis, capable d&#39;examiner les taux d&#39;occupation de la RAM et de différents points de montage disque (attention, il ne fonctionnera pas sous Windows). </p>

<p>Un serveur central (que vous allez réaliser en Rails) permet à l&#39;administrateur de définir facilement et rapidement son parc (salles, machines dans ces salles avec leurs IP…), et va interroger à intervalles réguliers ces machines pour vérifier qu&#39;elles sont actives, et leur agent opérationnel. Les agents examinent à intervalle régulier leur machine, et font spontanément remonter au serveur tout incident (taux d&#39;utilisation trop élevé). Le serveur fournit, dans son interface web, une page de supervision en temps réel, qui représente « graphiquement » le parc, et utilise AJAX pour ajuster fréquemment l&#39;aspect des machines représentées, afin de traduire les éventuels incidents (ou terminaisons d&#39;incident). </p>

<p>Définition simple de parc </p>

<p>L&#39;administrateur doit pouvoir injecter son parc dans le système : salles et machines dans ces salles. Une machine, pour les besoins de notre outil, peut se limiter à son nom et son IP, mais si vous voulez vous lâcher, libre à vous. </p>

<p>La définition du parc doit pouvoir se faire sans JavaScript, évidemment. Tout le système doit d&#39;ailleurs être accessible, et JavaScript/AJAX ne sont là que pour rendre le tout bien plus confortable. On doit donc avoir des liens et des formulaires classiques pour ajouter une salle, ajouter des machines dans une salle, et maintenir tout ça par la suite (retrait ou déplacement de machine, retrait de salle, etc.). </p>

<p>Une salle a simplement un nom : pour notre outil, on se fout un peu de sa capacité, son emplacement, etc. </p>

<p>À intervalle régulier (par exemple toutes les minutes), le serveur va vérifier que les machines inscrites dans le système sont joignables, et que l&#39;agent y est opérationnel. Pour cela, il se connecte sur l&#39;agent et envoie le message idoine. </p>

<p>Affichage de supervision </p>

<p>Il s&#39;agit d&#39;un écran affichant graphiquement le parc, qui se met à jour régulièrement pour refléter les incidents éventuels en cours. </p>

<p>Les salles sont représentées sous forme de boîtes rectangulaires. Dans ces boîtes, les machines concernées sont affichées (boîte obtenue par CSS, grand icône d&#39;ordinateur, comme vous voulez…) Tout incident en cours pour une machine est affiché en association avec celle-ci (icône plus petit superposé à, ou au-dessous de, la représentation de la machine) L&#39;écran doit pouvoir se mettre à jour régulièrement, de façon accessible. Si JavaScript n&#39;est pas actif, on aura donc recours à une équivalent HTTP de l&#39;en-tête Refresh, grâce à l&#39;élément </p>

<p>. Dans le cas contraire, on utilisera AJAX pour éviter de rafraîchir toute la page : la réponse nous indiquera alors uniquement les incidents terminés ou apparus depuis la dernière consultation, et on ajustera dynamiquement le contenu de la page. </p>

<p>Toujours dans un souci d&#39;accessibilité, toute image doit bien sûr avoir une contrepartie textuelle (qui n&#39;est pas forcément visible avec les images activées, mais doit l&#39;être en images désactivées ou dans une consultation textuelle de la page). </p>

<p>Il est inutile de rafraîchir trop souvent, sauf peut-être pendant les tests : un intervalle d&#39;une minute est a priori amplement suffisant (en revanche, au-delà de 5 minutes on n&#39;est vraiment plus « temps réel »). </p>

<p>Remontée d&#39;incidents et historisation </p>

<p>Les incidents parviennent au serveur de deux façons : </p>

<p>Il les détecte lui-même lors de vérifications périodiques de connectivité des agents, comme vu en section II.2. Les agents font spontanément remonter des incidents au travers d&#39;une requête HTTP de création REST appropriée, comme indiqué dans leur documentation. Le serveur doit historiser les incidents, ce qui suppose qu&#39;un incident a au moins les propriétés suivantes : </p>

<p>Machine concernée Type d&#39;incident (ex. RAM trop basse, espace libre trop bas sur un point de montage, connectivité défaillante) Propriétés complémentaires (ex. RAM restante, espace disque restant, etc.) Moment de détection (date/heure) Moment de résolution (constatation d&#39;incident terminé) Pour la connectivité, c&#39;est le serveur lui-même qui crée l&#39;incident et, lorsqu&#39;il constate qu&#39;elle fonctionne alors qu&#39;un incident est actif (détection sans résolution), le marque comme résolu. Pour les autres types d&#39;incidents, qui sont remontés spontanément par les agents, ces derniers gardent trace des incidents qu&#39;ils ont signalés et notifient automatiquement leur résolution lorsqu&#39;ils la constatent. </p>

<p>Cette historisation ouvre la voie au calcul de durées de résolution, de durées totales d&#39;incident, etc. On peut imaginer pas mal de statistiques. </p>

<p>Partie authentifiée </p>

<p>L&#39;application dispose d&#39;un ou plusieurs comptes utilisateur, tous administrateurs, et il est nécessaire de s&#39;authentifier pour pouvoir accéder à toute opération modificatrice, donc principalement la définition du parc. En revanche, la supervision, l&#39;interrogation manuelle, les éventuelles statistiques, etc. sont accessibles en anonyme. </p>

<p>Interrogation manuelle d&#39;une machine </p>

<p>Depuis l&#39;écran de supervision, il doit être possible d&#39;interroger manuellement l&#39;état d&#39;une machine en s&#39;adressant à son agent. On peut simplement vérifier sa connectivité, ou demander l&#39;état de la RAM ou d&#39;un point de montage. Cela peut avoir lieu dans un écran à part ou en AJAX (ceci dit, ça doit pouvoir être utilisable sans AJAX, comme d&#39;habitude). </p>

<p>Le contrôleur sollicité va se connecter à l&#39;agent comme il le ferait pour vérifier la connectivité, mais invoquer d&#39;autres commandes (voir la documentation), créer ou résoudre l&#39;incident éventuel comme il le ferait lors des vérifications périodiques normales, et signifier le résultat à la partie client.</p>
 title : The blisscarott Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Projet de gestion de parc informatique en rails</p>
 title : The blissinsia Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Vous allez réaliser un système de supervision en temps réel (ou presque) de parc informatique. Le principe est le suivant : </p>

<p>Chaque machine supervisée du parc a un « agent » déployé dessus, qui tourne en arrière-plan. Il s&#39;agit d&#39;un script Ruby que je vous fournis, capable d&#39;examiner les taux d&#39;occupation de la RAM et de différents points de montage disque (attention, il ne fonctionnera pas sous Windows). Un serveur central (que vous allez réaliser en Rails) permet à l&#39;administrateur de définir facilement et rapidement son parc (salles, machines dans ces salles avec leurs IP…), et va interroger à intervalles réguliers ces machines pour vérifier qu&#39;elles sont actives, et leur agent opérationnel. Les agents examinent à intervalle régulier leur machine, et font spontanément remonter au serveur tout incident (taux d&#39;utilisation trop élevé). Le serveur fournit, dans son interface web, une page de supervision en temps réel, qui représente « graphiquement » le parc, et utilise AJAX pour ajuster fréquemment l&#39;aspect des machines représentées, afin de traduire les éventuels incidents (ou terminaisons d&#39;incident).</p>

 title : The boling-for-batches Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Boling For Batches v1.0.2Plugin for RailsI often need to execute really large computations on really large data sets.  I usually end up writing a rake task to do it, which calls methods in my models.  But something about the process bugged me.  Each time I had to re-implement my &#39;batching code&#39; that allowed me to not chew up GB after GB of memory due to klass.find(:all, :include =&gt; :everything_under_the_sun). Re-implementation of the same logic over and over across many projects is not very DRY, so I got out my blow torch and lit it up.  The difficulty was that the part that was different each time I batched was at the center of the code, right in the middle of the batch loop.  But I didn&#39;t let that stop me! </p>

<p>InstallSVN: </p>

<p>svn checkout http://boling-for-batches.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/boling_for_batchesRails Plugin: </p>

<p>./script/plugin install http://boling-for-batches.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/boling_for_batchesExample  #Setup your new batch, and tell it what options to use, and what class to run batches of
<br/>  batch = BolingForBatches::Batch.new(:klass =&gt; Payment, :select =&gt; &quot;DISTINCT transaction_id&quot;, :batch_size =&gt; 50, :order =&gt; &#39;transaction_id&#39;)
<br/>  
<br/>  #Run a specific instance method on each record in each batch, and send the rest of the params to that method.
<br/>  batch.run(:remove_duplicates, false, true, true)
<br/>  
<br/>  #Print the results!
<br/>  batch.print_resultsConfigurationOptions for the initializer (Batch.new) method are: </p>

<p>  :klass         - Usage: :klass =&gt; MyClass
<br/>                    Required, as this is the class that will be batched</p>

<p>  :include       - Usage: :include =&gt; [:assoc]
<br/>                    Optional</p>

<p>  :select       - Usage: :select =&gt; &quot;DISTINCT field_name&quot;
<br/>                              or
<br/>                         :select =&gt; &quot;field1, field2, field3&quot;</p>

<p>  :order         - Usage: :order =&gt; &quot;field DESC&quot;</p>

<p>  :conditions    - Usage: :conditions =&gt; [&quot;field1 is not null and field2 = ?&quot;, x]</p>

<p>  :verbose       - Usage: :verbose =&gt; &#39;yes&#39; or &#39;no&#39;
<br/>                    Sets verbosity of output
<br/>                  Default: yes (if not provided)
<br/>                  
<br/>  :batch_size    - Usage: :batch_size =&gt; x
<br/>                    Where x is some number.
<br/>                    How many AR Objects should be processed at once?
<br/>                  Default: 50 (if not provided)
<br/>                  
<br/>  :last_batch   - Usage: :last_batch =&gt; x
<br/>                    Where x is some number.
<br/>                    Only process up to and including batch #x.
<br/>                      Batch numbers start at 0 for the first batch.
<br/>                  Default: won&#39;t be used (no limit if not provided)
<br/>                  
<br/>  :first_batch  - Usage: first_batch =&gt; x
<br/>                    Where x is some number.
<br/>                    Begin processing batches beginning at batch #x.
<br/>                      Batch numbers start at 0 for the first batch.
<br/>                  Default: won&#39;t be used (no offset if not provided)                     </p>

<p>Output       Interpreting the output: </p>

<p>   [O] means the batch was skipped due to an offset.    [L] means the batch was skipped due to a limit.    [P] means the batch is processing.    [C] means the batch is complete. and yes... it was a coincidence.  This class is not affiliated with &#39;one laptop per child&#39; LicenseCopyright (c) 2008 Peter H. Boling, released under the MIT license 
<br/>	 </p>

<p>Or in other words have fun, and don&#39;t blame me!</p>

 title : The bonnie-64 Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Bonnie, originally written in 1989-90 when I was in the employ of the Oxford English Dictionary project, is a C-language benchmark measuring the performance of Unix filesystems.  There is some discussion at http://www.textuality.com/bonnie. </p>

<p>There is another version of Bonnie, Bonnie++, developed by Russell Coker, which appears both at http://www.coker.com.au/bonnie++/ and http://sourceforge.net/projects/bonnie/ - it is in C++ and includes many tests that Bonnie doesn&#39;t.  It works around the 32-bit limit by scattering the data across multiple files. </p>

<p>Bonnie64 is a slight rev of the original Bonnie, designed to run on 64-bit computers.  Also the output is a bit more useful since it reports in M/sec rather than K/sec.  Its construction is discussed at my blog see http://www.tbray.org/ongoing/When/200x/2004/11/16/Bonnie64 and http://www.tbray.org/ongoing/When/200x/2005/12/07/ZFS</p>

 title : The box2dx Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Box2DX is a C# port of Box2D - Erin Catto&#39;s 2D Physics Engine. You can find original C++ version on www.box2d.org </p>

<p>Collision: </p>

<p>Continuous collision detection. Contact callbacks: add, persist, remove. Convex polyons and circles. Multiple shapes per body. One-shot contact manifolds. Incremental sweep-and-prune broadphase. Efficient pair management. Fast broadphase AABB queries. Collision groups and categories. </p>

<p>Physics: </p>

<p>Continuous physics with time of impact island solver. Persistent body-joint-contact graph. Island solution and sleep management. Contact, friction, and restitution. Stable stacking with a linear-time solver. Revolute, prismatic, distance, pulley, gear, and mouse joints. Joint limits, motors, and friction. Momentum decoupled position correction. Fairly accurate reaction forces/impulses. </p>

<p>System: </p>

<p>Centralized tuning parameters. Pure .NET 2.0 library. </p>

<p>Documentation: - </p>

<p>Testbed: </p>

<p>OpenGL with Tao.Freeglut Graphical user interface Easily switch between tests using GUI Test framework for easily adding new tests Mouse picking and the bomb! VCS9 project files </p>

<p>The Library is free for commercial use and open source under the ZLib License.</p>

 title : The brightcontent Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Bright Content is a lightweight, RESTful [1] content management platform written in Python from reusable components. Its most common use is as a Weblog engine. It is based on a simple, coherent philosophy for content architecture, and reuses sound Web standards and software components to avoid over-architecture and code bloat.   </p>

<p>Bright Content offers many of the usual features of Weblog engines and other content engines, but its basic operation and plug-in model is based on the WSGI standard for Python Web components. Many existing WSGI components can be plugged directly into Bright Content in order to enhance its operation, and Bright Content also has a set of specialized components for common content needs. </p>

<p>Bright Content also builds on the Atom Syntax, Atom Protocol, and an XML data flow. XML is used modestly (e.g. not for configuration) and is intended as much as possible not to get in the way. Built-in templates are XSLT for now, but support for plug-ins providing other templating systems is in the near-term roadmap. </p>

<p>[1] RESTful -- designed with well-known principles of well-behaved Web applications.</p>

 title : The btpd-webui Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>BTPDwebui is a simple webui for the Bittorrent Protocol Daemon (btpd).  It allows the user to add, start, stop, and delete torrents from btpd, as well as view the status of current torrents.</p>
 summary : <p>Important note: development (if any) is now focused on hxMotion branch. It currently compiles to Javascript and Haxe&gt;SWF9, and once it&#39;s more complete I&#39;ll keep an updated SWC export for use with AS3. It&#39;s neat to use it with haxe, though, I love the syntactic sugar that &#39;using&#39; keyword allows for, such as: ball.tween({x:200}).start.queue().back(); </p>

<p>This project is in public repository since Sep 2008. It&#39;s been created in the first half of 2007, while flex sdk was still in beta. First deployed project using it was an interface for BBC Scottland, dating back to July 2007. So don&#39;t dare calling this &#39;new&#39;, please. </p>

<p>&quot;If God does not exist, everything is permitted&quot; - Fyodor Dostoevsky, in The Brothers Karamazov </p>

<p>&quot;&#39;Everything is permitted&#39; does not mean that nothing is forbidden...&quot; / &quot;One can be virtuous through a whim&quot; - Albert Camus, in The Absurd Man </p>

<p>BTween is aimed to provide both a very strict and verbose syntax - which motivated me to write this api - and a very loose, quick&#39;n&#39;dirty one. </p>

<p>First one is intended to comply with the complexity of current flash/flex applications, which will benefit from the tighter use of good OOP practices and patterns. Second is given to the simple uses we still may have of flash - you certainly won&#39;t want to loose time creating a fully standardized and documented application when coding a simple banner, for example. I strongly disrecommend the use of long chains of tweens in a single line for a serious application, as well as I recommend the use of the regular Event model in most cases, and the instantiation of BTween objects instead of the &quot;static calls&quot; way. </p>

<p>So this looks good to me: </p>

<p>var tween:BTween = new BTween();
<br/>tween.queue(trace,&quot;I&#39;m a callback&quot;);
<br/>tween.add({target:blueBall,y:100});
<br/>tween.add({target:redBall,y:200});
<br/>tween.start();While this might be good for a banner that will be sent to trash after a couple of days of use </p>

<p>BTween.make().start({target:blueball,y:10},{target:redBall,y:200}).queue(doSomething);With this being an intermediary approach: </p>

<p>var tween:BTween = new BTween();
<br/>tween.queue(doSomething);
<br/>tween.start({target:blueball,y:10},{target:redBall,y:200});This flexibility haven&#39;t made of BTween a sumo fighter, though. The minimal footprint is around 3k, making it light enough to be used in banners or other weight-sensitive uses. The API is also meant to be easily extensible, you can actually code your own extension in a few minutes, implementing IProperty or ISequenceable interfaces. </p>

<p>BTween is in ALPHA state, though I&#39;ve been using it for almost an year, and even its design is being improved each day. If anyone is interested in helping, I&#39;d be happy to give commit rights. Just contact me. </p>

<p>Please send your thoughts to pedromoraes@gmail.com. No beginner support requests please.</p>

 title : The buildobjects Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>buildobjects provides a number of java classes that allow you to code your build process in  a truly object oriented fashion. It is not forcing you into a certain way of structuring your code and projects. Instead it aims at providing useful building blocks. </p>

<p>The rationale for using java was the availability of the full tool support to th build script. So when using buildobjects you get completetion, search for usage, and a fully featured debugger. </p>

<p>Getting StartedDownload and install buildobjectsGet the buildobjects-dep.jar from the downnloads section.  Put the file into the local file system and create and an alias or a script to run it: alias bo=&quot;java -jar /pathtobuildobjects/buildobjects-dep.jar&quot;Make sure that you are using java 6. </p>

<p>Getting the project set upThe project to be built looks somewhat like this: </p>

<p>|-- build
<br/>|   +-- Build.java
<br/>|-- lib
<br/>|   |-- some.jar
<br/>|   +-- more_dependencies
<br/>|-- src
<br/>|   +-- Sources go here...
<br/>+-- test
<br/>    +-- Test srouces go here...The build older contains the actual build script. A minimal build script looks like this: </p>

<p>import org.buildobjects.BuildBase;
<br/>import org.buildobjects.artifacts.Classes;
<br/>import org.buildobjects.artifacts.FileLocation;
<br/>import org.buildobjects.artifacts.Location;
<br/>import org.buildobjects.projectmodel.JavaModule;</p>

<p>public class Build extends BuildBase {
<br/>    private JavaModule module;</p>

<p>    public Build() {
<br/>        Location location = new FileLocation(&quot;.&quot;);
<br/>        Classes libraries = location.jarDir(&quot;lib&quot;);
<br/>        module = new JavaModule(tasks, location, libraries);
<br/>    }</p>

<p>    public void build() {        
<br/>        build.publish(module.publishable());
<br/>    }
<br/>    
<br/>    public static void main(String[] args) {
<br/>        new Build().build();
<br/>    }It is a good practice to have a separate project in your IDE setup for the builds. This includes the buildobjects-dep.jar on the classpath. </p>

<p>How to run?To trigger your build form the IDE you can just execute the main method in the buildfile.  To run a build from the command line the buildfile has to be compiled. Fortunately the buildobjects Tasklets do the job for you: </p>

<p>bo -source build BuildAfter running the build you will see a new directory appearing: </p>

<p>|-- target
<br/>|   |-- 20081106-145511-build.1
<br/>|   |   |-- SUCCEEDED
<br/>|   |   |-- index.html
<br/>|   |   +-- testproject-simple
<br/>|   |       |-- test-results.txt
<br/>|   |       +-- testproject-simple.jar
<br/>|   |-- environment.json
<br/>|   +-- index.htmlThe target folder is associated with the build environment in which the builds happen. It has an index.html listing all the builds (as well as a json keeping things like the last buildnumber. For each build a new folder is created, that has all the buildresults. </p>

<p>To see what this build actually published have a look at the JavaModule class. It is expected that projects will define their own JavaModule class. If it is put in the build folder it will be compiled when the build is run. </p>

<p>The example use here is available via svn: http://buildobjects.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/example/testproject-simple.</p>

 title : The bulk-loader Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>BulkLoader is a minimal library written in Actionscript 3 (AS3) that aims to make loading and managing complex loading requirements easier and faster. BulkLoader takes a more dynamic, less architecture heavy aproach. Few imports and making heavy use of AS3&#39;s dynamic capabilities, BulkLoader has a one-liner feel that doesn&#39;t get in your way. </p>

<p>BulkLoader hides the complexity of loading different data types in AS3 and provides a unified interface for loading, accessing and events notification for different types of content. </p>

<p>This library is licensed under an open source MIT license. Features: </p>

<p>Connection pooling.  Unified interface for different loading types.  Unified progress notification.  Events for individual items and as groups.  Priority   Stop and resuming individually as well as in bulk.  Cache management.  Statistics about loading (latency, speed, average speed).  Various kinds on progress indication: ratio (items loaded / items to load), bytes , and weighted percentage.   Configurable number of retries.  Configurable logging.   Various assest types (XML, NetStreams, Swfs, Images, Sound, Text Files) </p>

<p>Design goals: </p>

<p> Minimal imports.  Few method to learn.  Consistent interface, regardless of content type. </p>

<p>BulkLoader gracefully handles progress notification in these use cases: </p>

<p> Few connections to open: bytes total can be used instantly.  Many connections opened: progress by ratio  Many connections opened for data of widely varying sizes: progress by weight.</p>
 summary : <p>Bulkmail is a simple bulk mailing library in Ruby. Also included is a command line utility for sending bulk mail using a single command.</p>

 title : The bumpslide Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>NOTE: I know longer have any intention of maintaining this project. Unfortunately, I just don&#39;t do anymore Ruby on Rails front-end work. If you have sufficient interest and would like to take this project over, please contact me. Thank you. </p>

<p>Tim Harper </p>

<p> </p>

<p>WHY BUNDLE-FU IS SPECIALWeb 2.0 sites have lots of tiny javascript/css files, which causes one extra round trip per file to the server and back!  This is bad!  Bundle-fu throws it all up into a big package and sends it out all at once.   </p>

<p>Bundle-fu can speed your load time up around 50%. </p>

<p>It: </p>

<p>Does not require a separate config file Automatically regenerates the bundle if you modify an included file, or change the include order. Is easily bypassed by passing &quot;?bundle_fu=false&quot; into your page (including assets separately vs bundled).  It does not affect other users of your site, and stays bypassed for the your session only.  Bundle-fu makes debugging fun! Is optimized for production mode (only generates the bundle file once when the server is first started). Puts the bundles in javascripts/cache and stylesheets/cache, so it&#39;s easy to ignore with subversion. Rewrites relative URLs in your CSS files, so you&#39;ll never have broken images. Minimizes your javascripts by default using the Ruby Version of JSMin.  Optionally, if you install PackR, it will automatically use that instead. No additional requests on your rails application - bundled files are served as static files. Supports multiple combinations of JS/CSS, using the :name parameter USAGE / INSTALLATIONStep 1Install this plugin </p>

<p>git clone git://github.com/timcharper/bundle-fu.git vendor/plugins/bundle-fu &amp;&amp; rm -rf vendor/plugins/bundle-fu/.gitStep 2Put the following around your stylesheets/javascripts (note it works with any method of including assets!): </p>

<p>  
<br/>    ...

 title : The bunky Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Bunny the FuzzerA closed loop, high-performance, general purpose protocol-blind fuzzer for C programs. </p>

<p>Uses compiler-level integration to seamlessly inject precise and reliable instrumentation hooks into the traced program. These hooks enable the fuzzer to receive real-time feedback on changes to the function call path, call parameters, and return values in response to variations in input data. </p>

<p>This architecture makes it possible to significantly improve the coverage of the testing process without a noticeable performance impact usually associated with other attempts to peek into run-time internals. </p>

<p>Bunny is currently known to support Linux, FreeBSD, OpenBSD, and Cygwin on IA32 and IA64 systems. </p>

 title : The bushel Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>OverviewBushel provides utility classes for Ant Ivy that allow a developer to use a directory of OSGi bundles as a dependency repository. It does this through a custom metadata parser that converts a MANIFEST.MF file into a valid ivy.xml. The aim is to assist IDE-free OSGi development and continuous integration best practice.  </p>

<p>Current limitations are that Import-Package and Export-Package parameters in the manifest file are ignored, however Require-Bundle is honoured. </p>

<p>ExampleThe Bushel example bundle is based on the Eclipse PDE/New Plug-in Project/OSGi Simple LogService Example. </p>

<p>It includes all the Ant and Ivy scripts required to compile and run the bundle, and can be used as a template for your own project. </p>

<p>To use the Ant script, you must provide the path to the Eclipse home dir (the parent dir of the plugins/ dir) using -Declipse.home=/path/to/eclipse. It provides the following targets: </p>

<p>ant compile - Compile your bundle using Ivy to generate the classpath. ant bundle - Package your bundle jar ready for deployment. ant run - Run your bundle in equinox in console mode. Try ss, or diag 2, or help, and then finally close, to exit. </p>

<p>TODOImport-Package/Export-Package support. Examples with other OSGi containers (Felix, Knoplerfish etc). Eclipse Update site support. Check out the project Issues for more detail. </p>

 title : The byteplay Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>byteplay lets you convert Python code objects into equivalent objects which are easy to play with, and lets you convert those objects back into living Python code objects. It&#39;s useful for applying crazy transformations on Python functions, and is also useful in learning Python byte code intricacies. It currently works with Python 2.4 and 2.5. </p>

<p>It&#39;s similar in purpose to Michael Hudson&#39;s bytecodehacks, and can be compared with Phillip J. Eby&#39;s peak.util.assembler. </p>

<p>I think it&#39;s pretty reliable - Python&#39;s complete test suite continues to pass after you use byteplay to disassemble all function objects and assemble them again! </p>

<p>Download it from http://byteplay.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/byteplay.py!</p>
