 title : The c5-db-migration Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Latest Version: 0.9.9-m3 (check out the new check goal!) </p>

<p>OverviewThe Carbon Five Database Migration framework and Maven plugin for Java provides a simple solution to the problem of managing discrete, incremental changes to databases over time across multiple environments.  Each migration is versioned and tracked when applied to the database.  Sensible defaults reduce the amount of necessary configuration, though the framework can be configured and extended.  Before this google code page, this framework was announced on our Community Blog. </p>

<p>Key Maven Plugin Goals</p>

<p>Goal  Description  db-migration:createCreate a new, empty database db-migration:migrateApply all pending migrations db-migration:resetDrop the existing database, create a new one, and apply all pending migrations db-migration:newCreate a new, empty migration script db-migration:checkCheck for pending migrations, fail the build if the db is not up to date </p>

<p>Sample Maven Plugin Configuration...</p>

<p>    com.carbonfive.db-support
<br/>    db-migration-maven-plugin
<br/>    RELEASE
<br/>    
<br/>        jdbc:mysql://localhost/myapp_test
<br/>        dev
<br/>        dev
<br/>    
<br/>    
<br/>        
<br/>            mysql
<br/>            mysql-connector-java
<br/>            5.1.6
<br/>        
<br/>    </p>

<p>    
<br/>        c5-public-repository
<br/>        http://mvn.carbonfive.com/public
<br/>    </p>

<p>...Other DetailsBy default, migrations are loaded from the directory src/main/db/migrations and follow the naming convention yyyymmddhhmmss_some_description.sql.  Version history is stored in the database in the schema_version table, which captures the version, date-applied, and how long it took for the migration to execute for each applied migration. </p>

<p>Supported DatabasesAll functionality is supported for MySQL, PostgreSQL, MS SQL Server, HSQL, and H2Database, though the migrate functionality is likely to work with many other database systems.  Create/drop/reset are less likely to work out of the box.  Our goal is to support all of the major database systems and we&#39;re eager to hear how it works with other systems. </p>

<p>DocumentationCheck out the Maven Plugin Guide if you&#39;re interested in manually triggering database updates.  If you want to embed the migration framework in your application, check out the Application Embedding Guide.</p>

<p> which is how an SQL DB works </p>

<p> clickity click </p>

<p> its done. </p>

<p>Feature ListEasy to use Model-View-Controller approach Complete database abstraction layer provided by Creole (MySQL, pgSQL etc..) Object Relation Model (ORM) that eliminates the need to write SQL Simple yet powerful template engine with the ability to specify custom engine XML template builder for writing XML documents (example: RSS) Built-in translation support to make your application available in multiple languages Built-in dynamic URL re-writing Directory indexer with customizable templates and icons for listing contents of directories Similar syntax and concepts to Ruby on Rails AJAX support Memcached and APC integration (not yet in svn) Flex/Weborb integration (not yet in svn) Need information?Visit the Cabbie wiki for more information on how to install and use Cabbie for your web applications. </p>

 title : The cachecontrol Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Why?There are many caching frameworks out there - this isn&#39;t one of them. Instead it aims to make it as simple as possible to use caches without worrying about thread safety and cache invalidation or having to reinvent the wheel and repeat common mistakes. </p>

<p>LightweightIt&#39;s deliberately not heavyweight or comprehensive. There&#39;s no need. We want to make sure that simplicity outs. The APIs are named like a Cash Machine. Likewise, control of caches is split up - one set of APIs for those asking for caches, and another or those controlling them. It should be blindingly simple to write your own wrappers for your favourites. There are no dependencies apart from Java 5! </p>

<p>IoCInversion of Control is a powerful paradigm in helping to write easily tested, highly coherent, loose couplings of objects. We&#39;ve designed this API to best suit Constructor Injection. We also make use of a closure-like approach to visit things! </p>

<p>Where did Cache Control come from?Inspired by the humane interfaces and compelling simplicity of projects such as Ruby, XStream, Hamcrest and Rehersal. Many thanks to Joe Walnes for showing us the &#39;BetterHashtable&#39; - a lesson never forgotten... Like all good libraries, this one&#39;s come out of a real problem we once had to debug for days!</p>
 title : The cachedassets Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>CachedAssetsRails plugin to intended to help reduce the number of HTTP requests when loading static assets like stylesheets and JavaScript files. </p>

<p>InstallationTo get the latest version: </p>

<p>  script/plugin install http://cachedassets.googlecode.com/svn/trunkUsageInstead of using the default Rails helpers like </p>

<p>  &lt;%= javascript_include_tag :defaults %&gt;
<br/>  &lt;%= stylesheet_link_tag &#39;scaffold&#39; %&gt;use: </p>

<p>  &lt;%= cached_javascript_include_tag :defaults %&gt;
<br/>  &lt;%= cached_stylesheet_link_tag &#39;scaffold&#39; %&gt;The key here is to have as few of these statements as possible because the plugin will  make a single asset from the list of sources. </p>

<p>So, if you might have something like: </p>

<p>  &lt;%= javascript_include_tag :defaults %&gt;
<br/>  &lt;%= javascript_include_tag &#39;lightbox&#39; %&gt;
<br/>  &lt;%= javascript_include_tag &#39;yui/yahoo-min&#39;, &#39;yui/event-min&#39;, &#39;yui/treeview-min&#39; %&gt;then you want to combine them into a single statement, like so: </p>

<p>  &lt;%= cached_javascript_include_tag :defaults, &#39;lightbox&#39;, &#39;yui/yahoo-min&#39;, &#39;yui/event-min&#39;, &#39;yui/treeview-min&#39; %&gt;</p>

 summary : <p>Cairngen is an open source code generation utility which simplifies the development process when building Flex applications with the Adobe Cairngorm Micro-architecture.  </p>

<p>Cairngen helps facilitate design consistency and best practices within large collaborative team environments. All code is generated from class templates which can easily be customized to meet the needs of your specific Cairngorm implementation. Cairngen eliminates the redundant, error prone &quot;copy / paste&quot; work flow often associated with creating new Events and Commands in a Cairngorm project. With Cairngen you can accomplish in seconds what could normally take hours to accomplish manually. </p>

 summary : <p>OverviewA bindings compatible NSControl subclass which draws a calendar much like the one sported by the iPhone. The project also includes AFWeekView designed to eliminate having to use checkboxes to represent days. </p>

<p>  </p>

<p>AFCalendarControl exposes five bindings: </p>

<p>AFCurrentMonthBinding, the month to display NSContentBinding; an enumerable collection AFContentDatesBinding; bound to the model subpath for the date property, expects an NSDate object NSSelectedIndexBinding; the index of the selected object in the object returned by NSContentBinding AFDateHighlightedBinding; bound to the model subpath, expects a BOOL wrapped in an NSNumber. If set the control will draw an indicator below the date&#39;s day number. DependenciesMac OS X Leopard 10.5 Objective-C 2.0 Xcode 3.0 CalendarControl is dependent on a framework (AmberKitAdditions) contained inside another one of my projects Amber found at http://code.google.com/p/amber-framework which must be available at compile time.  </p>

<p>Using the ControlThe easiest way to use CalendarControl is to instead download Amber.framework which contains all my custom UI controls and the AppKit additions required to use them. </p>

<p>Otherwise you can download the code for this project alone using an svn:external property to pull the &#39;code&#39; subdirectory, i.e. http://calendarcontrol.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/application/code, you could also pull the &#39;code&#39; directory from a branch or tag. </p>

<p>Building the ControlIf you checkout the entire project (see &quot;Repository Structure&quot; below) and are building it from source then the Xcode project must be able to find the Amber Xcode project file. </p>

<p>It expects to find the Amber working copy at the same level as it&#39;s own working directory. It must also be able to link the framework; the two projects should either share their build products directory, or you must set custom header search paths. See here http://lists.apple.com/archives/Xcode-users/2008/Sep/msg00268.html for more information. </p>

<p>def exp_fun( start_num, end_num )
<br/>    ret_val = 1
<br/>    
<br/>    start_num.upto( end_num ) do |num|
<br/>        ret_val = ret_val * num
<br/>    end
<br/>    
<br/>    return ret_val.to_s.size
<br/>end</p>

In testing, the Rails app showed to still be responsive while the threads were sleeping (granted, the trivial code).  More anecdotal production use notes are still required, tho. <p>can has chat is a plugin for Ruby on Rails that allows you to easily plugin messaging functionality to your app using XMPP4R.  The plugin uses a separate dRuby server to receive chat events, and can optionally use a provided Mongrel handler script to use pseudo-server-push style communication that eases the load that server polling (also supported) would cause. </p>

<p>can has chat requires the JSON and XMPP4R gems, and a working Jabber server (http://www.ejabberd.im/, http://www.igniterealtime.org/projects/openfire/index.jsp).  Use of the server-push script requires Mongrel.  Chats with users of non-Jabber transports requires your Jabber server to be configured with transports for those networks, as well as a valid username and password for each chatter on that network.  If you wish to use anonymous jabber authentication, you&#39;ll need to use the trunk version of XMPP4R. </p>

<p>To install: </p>

<p>script/plugin install  http://canhaschat.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/canhaschat Example code: </p>

<p>Model: </p>

<p>class ChattyObject &lt; ActiveRecord::Base
<br/>  can_has_chat :namespace =&gt; &quot;My Multi-IM App&quot;,
<br/>                 :transports =&gt; {
<br/>                    :aim =&gt; :get_aim_nick,
<br/>                    :icq =&gt; [:get_icq_nick],
<br/>                    :yahoo =&gt; [:get_yahoo_nick, :get_yahoo_password]
<br/>                 }
<br/>   # methods
<br/>endView file: </p>

<p>&quot;/mychats/push?chat_id=#{@chat_id}&quot;) %&gt;</p>

<p>    : [] 
<br/>Controller: </p>

<p>class ChatController &lt; Application</p>

<p>   def chat()
<br/>      @chat_user = ChattyObject.find_by_id(params[:id])
<br/>      hash_of_transport_passwords_not_in_db = {
<br/>           :aim =&gt; &quot;someaimpassword&quot;,
<br/>           :icq =&gt; &quot;someicqpassword&quot;
<br/>      }
<br/>      @chat_id = @chat_user.start_chat(&quot;my_jabber_password&quot;, hash_of_transport_passwords_not_in_db)
<br/>   end
<br/>endMore usage examples and documentation are available in the project README.  </p>

<p>can has chat was initially created by the Indianapolis Star (http://www.indystar.com/, http://www.indy.com/) and has been released under the MIT License.</p>

 title : The canviz Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Canviz is a JavaScript library for drawing Graphviz graphs to a web browser canvas. More technically, Canviz is a JavaScript xdot renderer. It works in most modern browsers. </p>

<p>Using Canviz has advantages for your web application over generating and sending bitmapped images and imagemaps to the browser: </p>

<p>The server only needs to have Graphviz generate xdot text; this is faster than generating bitmapped images. Only the xdot text needs to be transferred to the browser; this is smaller than binary image data, and, if the browser supports it (which most do), the text can be gzip- or bzip2-compressed. The web browser performs the drawing, not the server; this reduces server load. The user can resize the graph without needing to involve the server; this is faster than having the server draw and send the graph in a different size. There is the potential to offer other features: </p>

<p>Mouse-over and mouse-out events to allow changing attributes (color, size, etc.) of portions of the graph Animations between graph states (see issue #26) A draggable interface like Google Maps for exploring large graphs (see issue #22) Please join me in the Canviz discussion group if you&#39;d like to use or help develop Canviz. Canviz can draw all the sample graphs provided with Graphviz and even supports other features not represented there, but Canviz is not finished yet and is still undergoing changes, sometimes drastic ones. I welcome you to use Canviz in your projects, but recommend that you also subscribe to the Canviz changes and Canviz issues groups so you can learn about changes to Canviz that might affect how you use it.</p>

 title : The captureme Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>SummaryCapture Me is a flexible screen capture and recording utility for Mac OS X which features a floating capture window, several saving options, and resize ability. </p>

<p>DetailsTo use the program, drag and resize the floating window to cover the area you want to capture. Then click in the window to capture the screenshot. You can resize it, copy it to the clipboard, and save it in a variety of formats and locations. Its behavior is customizable with respect to what happens after a capture. A newly added movie recording mode now allows up to a one minute long QuickTime movie (no sound) to be produced. </p>

<p>What advantage does Capture Me hold over the built in OS X screencapture facility? For some tasks, the answer is simple - there is none - the built in screen shot is elegant and easy to use. However, there are occasions when it&#39;s nice to be able to choose what file format your capture saves in, copy it to the clipboard without holding down four keys at once, or resize it on the fly. It&#39;s also common to want to take successive shots of the exact same position on the screen without moving the capture region at all, or make all your captures the same size. These tasks are trivial with Capture Me, but difficult at best with the built in utilities. Another possible use is as a floating capture pad - see the comment below for an example of one user who does this. </p>

<p>BuildingMake sure to check out the Building section of the Wiki for details before attempting to build this project.</p>

 title : The car-pool Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Caramel: a RedCloth enabler for RailsCaramel is a Ruby on Rails plugin that facilitates conversion of Textile input to HTML via RedCloth. </p>

<p>Problem:If you have a text field, say &#39;content&#39;, in your model and you intend to use that text field to contain the HTML for your web pages, then either the user of your web app must know HTML or else you&#39;ll have to convert the user&#39;s input from some other format like Textile. </p>

<p>The latter solution is quite attractive, and on top of that there is a great Ruby gem out there that does this conversion for you in a very easy way! It&#39;s called RedCloth and it works with Markdown as well. </p>

<p>But if you store the Textile markup in the database and convert it using RedCloth, you end up with a lot of processing overhead which will almost certainly get scary if your website gets popular. On the other hand, if you convert the Textile and then save the HTML to the database, you&#39;re back to forcing the user to learn HTML if he/she ever wants to go back to make edits. </p>

<p>Solution:Store BOTH Textile and HTML! Sure, this doubles the amount of data you have to store in the database, but storage is much more affordable than man-hours and per-request processing expenditures. </p>

<p>But who wants to go to the trouble of defining a before_save callback with RedCloth configs for each and every HTML-based column in your database? Enter Caramel. </p>

<p>Caramel is designed to make it very easy to instruct your model on which database columns will be used to store the Textile markup and which columns will be used to store the HTML. Caramel adds a method to ActiveRecord which looks for  certain naming conventions in your tables (or responds to the developer&#39;s configuration within the model) and then sets up a before_save callback based on your model. </p>

<p>Installation:Get to the command line, navigate to your plugins directory on your rails app, and then type in the following to install Caramel via anonymous checkout: </p>

<p>svn checkout http://caramel-plugin.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ caramelNote: This will install the very latest version of Caramel, which might be untested or even unstable. As stable, tested versions become available, I will make an effort to post milestones here. Until then, please feel free to use the trunk version, which as of writing seems very stable although untested. </p>

<p>Please also see the Usage section below, since you&#39;ll have to make some accommodations in your database. </p>

<p>Usage:For any columns in your database that you would like use for HTML, simply create a column for Textile storage and a column for HTML storage: </p>

<p>create_table :web_pages do |t|
<br/>  t.column :content, :string
<br/>  t.column :content_html, :string
<br/>end...and in your model, Caramel takes care of the rest with 1 method call: </p>

<p>class WebPage &lt; ActiveRecord::Base
<br/>  caramelize
<br/>endIf you want more control over the way that Caramel behaves, of if you simply don&#39;t want to use Caramel&#39;s naming conventions, you can specify which columns to use (and how to treat them) as follows: </p>

<p>class WebPage &lt; ActiveRecord::Base
<br/>  caramelize
<br/>  @@html_columns = [
<br/>    Sweets::HTMLColumn.new(:raw =&gt; :my_textile_column, :cooked =&gt; :my_html_column, :redcloth_options =&gt; [:lite_mode])
<br/>  ]
<br/>endNote that :redcloth_options (optional) accepts any options that can be read as restrictions for RedCloth.new. </p>

<p>Development Roadmap:The biggest changes I would like to make in the near future are as follows: </p>

<p>Write some tests! I&#39;m new to test-driven-development and to testing as well, so although the current implementation has been tested well in production, I see the value of writing a separate test suite and intend to get one rolling in order to facilitate other items in the dev roadmap:  Have the caramelize method accept a block for config rather than reading configuration from a @@ class variable (see activescaffold plugin for a clean example of what I&#39;m talking about). Write an installer for the plugin which generates a migration file and a model file for storing all the HTML in a single table with polymorphic associations instead of requiring that the Textile and the HTML both be in separate columns for each table.</p>

 summary : <p>Lagniappe based Replicated State Machine </p>

<p>- Aardvark is a new BFT protocol which aims to provide high performance in presence of faults by optimizing the cases where Byzantine faults are common. </p>

<p>- Combining ideas of Aardvark with Lagniappe would yield a better performant system in presence of Byzantine faults. </p>

<p>Lagniappe - http://code.google.com/p/lagniappe/</p>

 summary : <p>SADI, and it&#39;s first implementation in CardioSHARE, are a novel Web Services framework that dynamically generates RDF graphs by accessing Web Services.  Web Service discovery is achieved by registering the type of relationship (i.e. the predicate) that the Web Service creates between its input data and its output data. </p>

<p>See an early prototype application demo.  Note that THERE IS NO DATABASE/TRIPLESTORE under these demos!  All data is being discovered dynamically by the SADI system through &quot;semantic interpretation&quot; of the query, followed by discovery of Semantic Web Services capable of generating the data required to resolve the query, automated execution of the discovered Services, retrieval of the resulting triples, and finally resolution of the query using a normal SPARQL query engine (at the moment we are using Pellet). </p>

 title : The cashbookonrails Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Cassia is a .NET library for accessing the native Windows Terminal Services API. It can be used from C#, Visual Basic.NET, or any other .NET language. </p>

<p>What can I do with it?Cassia supports the following operations on both local and remote terminal servers: </p>

<p>Enumerating terminal sessions and reporting session information including connection state, user name, client name, client display details, client-reported IP address, and client build number (WTSEnumerateSessions, WTSQuerySessionInformation, and friends) Logging off a session (WTSLogoffSession) Disconnecting a session (WTSDisconnectSession) Displaying a message box in a session and getting a response from the user (WTSSendMessage) Enumerating all processes (WTSEnumerateProcesses) Killing a process (WTSTerminateProcess) Shutting down or rebooting the server (WTSShutdownSystem) In addition, Cassia supports enumerating all terminal servers on a domain (WTSEnumerateServers). </p>

<p>So, how do I use it?ITerminalServicesManager manager = new TerminalServicesManager();
<br/>using (ITerminalServer server = manager.GetRemoteServer(&quot;your-server-name&quot;))
<br/>{
<br/>    server.Open();
<br/>    foreach (ITerminalServicesSession session in server.GetSessions())
<br/>    {
<br/>        Console.WriteLine(&quot;Session ID: &quot; + session.SessionId);
<br/>        Console.WriteLine(&quot;User: &quot; + session.UserAccount);
<br/>        Console.WriteLine(&quot;State: &quot; + session.ConnectionState);
<br/>        Console.WriteLine(&quot;Logon Time: &quot; + session.LoginTime);
<br/>    }
<br/>}A sample console application demonstrating all of Cassia&#39;s functionality is included in the distribution. </p>

<p>What platforms are supported?Cassia has been tested on Windows Server 2008 R2, Windows Server 2008, Windows Server 2003, Windows XP, and Windows Server 2000. It should work on Windows Vista as well. </p>

<p>But what about the standard .NET Framework library? (Or, why Cassia?)Well, support for the Terminal Services API in the .NET Framework is rather limited. Specifically, the only Terminal Services operations supported in the .NET library are: </p>

<p>Process.SessionId, which retrieves the Terminal Services session ID for a given process. ServiceBase.OnSessionChange, which provides notifications of changes to Terminal Services  sessions in a Windows service. SystemEvents.SessionSwitch, which provides notifications of changes to the session in which the application is running, provided that it is running a message loop. SystemInformation.TerminalServerSession, which tells you whether the calling process is running in a Terminal Services session. </p>

<p>Questions?Post to the mailing list: cassia-users@googlegroups.com. Bugs and feature requests can be submitted to the issue tracker.</p>

 title : The ccmonitor Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>IntroductionThere are lots of stuff we can do to make fun with Continuous Integration. We can make our computer shout &#39;build-------failed!&#39;, or we can make keyboard light blink randomly and quickly, or we just pop up a message to tell ourselves what&#39;s happened with build... </p>

<p>CC Monitor works on RSS of CruiseControl. It also can work on any CI Build Tool which provides RSS to report build status. The default rule to assert successful build is rss item title contains &#39;success&#39;, &#39;fixed&#39; or &#39;passed&#39;. </p>

<p>&quot;100% CLEAN&quot; Softpedia award </p>

<p>CC Monitor 1.2 releasedFixed bug: can&#39;t update widget panel UI when refresh widget panel has error </p>

<p>Changed: command &quot;say&quot; will not be asynchronism </p>

<p>Upgrade: can get committers while monitoring CruiseControl 2.7.x. </p>

<p>CC Monitor 1.1 releasedFixed bug: refresh settings page while configuring setting first time </p>

<p>Upgrade: default notifications including display message by Growl, say and display build status will be triggered asynchronism. </p>

<p>CC Monitor 1.0 releasedCC Monitor is upgraded to be a ruby internal DSL runner and needs ruby installed. For previous versions built on javascript eat too much memory and CPU time, the core of CC Monitor is rebuilt on ruby, and the widget will be only used as a view to display build status. After start CC Monitor, a ruby process will be running background. </p>

<p>The simplest script for monitoring a buildobserve build mingle =&gt; &#39;http://server/projects/minlge.rss&#39;This script will display build status icon on your widget. </p>

<p>How CC Monitor worksmap committer names: committers: For user name used to commit code is always abbreviated, you can redefine committer names by keyword &#39;committers&#39;. The user name should be unique in the script and should not be keywords of CC Monitor DSL and ruby, otherwise please put it into double-quotes, see example below. define build: build, def_build: Example: build mingle =&gt; &#39;http://server/projects/minlge.rss&#39;, mingle is build name and should be unique so that we can use it later, and it also works with ruby string, &#39;http://server/projects/minlge.rss&#39; is the rss feed of project. observe build status:  keep eyes on, keep one eye on, observe, observes: See example below. get build status and info: build: Except to defined build, this keyword can used to get build infos when it is inside block of observing build status. See example below. cant load: Example: say growl build message if cant load build new?: Return true if it is first time to get the recentest build. failed?: Return true if the recentest build is failed succeeded?: Return true if the recentest build is succeeded. loaded_error?: Return true if cant load build message: Build message string includes build name and build status. status: Return &#39;loaded error&#39;, &#39;succeeded&#39; or &#39;failed&#39; link: Return build report link url after loaded build. Return build rss url defined if cant load build committers: It is parsed from the recentest build rss item description. It is only supported well when observing CruiseControl.rb build now. refresh: Refresh build status, build will be refreshed automatically when observing it by keywords of observing build status. rss item title: Return the build rss item title. rss item description: Return the build rss item description. succeeded=: Reset build succeeded status, if the default parser can&#39;t parse your CruiseControl rss item title correctlly, you can check rss item title by yourself and use this to reset build result. send out build status message:  display: used to display build status icon or link on widget. Example: display build status icon, display build message link growl: used to send message to Growl Application. Example: tell growl build message say: same with &quot;say&quot; on Mac. Example: say build message, committers any other ruby code Custom CC Monitor scriptcommitters xli =&gt; lee, pwang =&gt; wpc, &quot;build&quot; =&gt; &quot;bu def&quot;</p>

<p>build mingle =&gt; &#39;http://server/projects/minlge.rss&#39;
<br/>build rubyworks =&gt; &#39;http://server/projects/rubyworks.rss&#39;</p>

<p># the build name followed monitoring keywords should be defined above
<br/>keep eyes on mingle, rubyworks do
<br/>  display build status icon</p>

<p>  tell growl build message if cant load build</p>

<p>  if build new?
<br/>    tell growl build message, committers
<br/>    if build succeeded?
<br/>      say &quot;stand clear, #{build message, committers}&quot; #use the message and committers info get from build as a string
<br/>    else
<br/>      say build message, committers
<br/>    end
<br/>  end
<br/>endprevious version 0.6</p>

 title : The ceibal-chess Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Ceibal-Chess(La versión en español de esta página se encuentra aquí) </p>

<p>This project is about creating a Chess activity for the Sugar environment to teach kids the basic rules of the game and allow them to play with one another and vs. the CPU. </p>

<p>Ceibal-Chess is a brand new Chess project that aims to produce a chess Activity for the Sugar and the XO </p>

<p>FeaturesFree as in Freedom (GPLv2) Designed from the ground up to work on the XO. Distributed as an Activity Bundle (.xo) Completely developed in Python + PyGame. Integration with GNU Chess. Player vs Player mode (in one Laptop, using DBus planned). Valid movements highlighting. Enemy movements highlighting. Portable: known to work on various Linux distros and Mac OS X. Easy to learn and use, without complex menus or options. The project is still in its early stages, with some known bugs open, but it&#39;s reaching an stage where heavy testing for bug-fixing would be extremely beneficial. </p>

<p>The source code is stored in google code. Anonymous checkout using Subversion is enabled, and the code includes an script for automatically creating the Activity Bundle which can be used to deploy the Activity on XO laptops. </p>

<p>You can contact the project administrator at asegovi AT gmail DOT com. There is also a google group, called ceibal-chess. </p>

<p>DownloadGet the developer beta over here! (recommended) If you have Subversion installed and like living on the edge, get the latest version by using the following command: svn checkout http://ceibal-chess.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ ceibal-chessRunning on WindowsDownload the developer beta (or get it via subversion), and double click the file called &quot;main&quot; (main.py), after having installed Python. </p>

<p>Running on Linux and Mac OS XGet the developer beta or the latest source code version using Subversion and run the main.py python script. </p>

<p>Installing on the XOFirst get the latest source code version for Linux or Mac OS X, then run the createbundle.sh BASH script. The created .xo bundle will be stored in the bundle/ directory. Copy this file to the XO and open it using Firefox or running the sugar-bundle-install command from the Terminal Activity. </p>

<p>Once installed, restart Sugar by pressing Control + Alt + Erase. The Ceibal-Chess icon should appear among the other activities. </p>

<p>It is also possible to run Ceibal-Chess from the Terminal Activity in the same way that it&#39;s run on Linux, provided you first unset the SUGAR_BUNDLE_PATH environment variable. </p>

<p>For more info, please visit: http://wiki.laptop.org/go/Ceibal_Jam </p>

<p>Hardware RequirementsDesigned to run on the XO, Ceibal-Chess has a small memory footprint and uses little CPU, saving battery life. The minimal hardware requirements to run Ceibal-Chess include: </p>

<p>500 MHz processor. 32MB RAM (64MB recommended). 20MB of free disk space (less when installed in the XO). Software RequirementsCeibal-Chess is developed in the Python programming language using the Pygame graphics library. These are the only requirements. </p>

<p>Python 2.x (not 3.0). Pygame 1.8.1. Notes: </p>

<p>Make sure you download the Pygame library version that matches your Python version. Linux users usually have Python installed and can get Pygame using apt-get or yum. XO users already have both dependencies -no need to install anything-. Windows and Mac users will have to get both packages.  NOT FOR PRODUCTIONCeibal-Chess is still a work in progress and as such, it&#39;s still not ready for prime time. You can expect the application to crash, dumping lots of debug files and might not be for the faint-hearted. However, if you like living on the edge, and want to see Ceibal-Chess reach production level soon, get the code and start playing! All feedback you send us will be really helpful for making Ceibal-Chess reach its best very soon! </p>

<p>More InformationFAQ (English)The English version of the FAQ is here: http://code.google.com/p/ceibal-chess/wiki/FaqEn </p>

<p>FAQ (Español)La versión en Español del FAQ se encuentra aquí: http://code.google.com/p/ceibal-chess/wiki/FAQSp. </p>

<p>Facebook Group (Español)Join us at the Facebook group, over here. </p>

<p>ScreenshotsMain Menu </p>

<p>In-Game</p>

 title : The cfast Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>IMPORTANT NOTE: This is NOT, the Primary Website for  CFAST Information. </p>

<p>You can find the main website at http://cfast.nist.gov </p>

<p>What is CFAST?The Consolidated Model of Fire and Smoke Transport, CFAST, is a computer program that fire investigators, safety officials, engineers, architects and builders can use to simulate the impact of past or potential fires and smoke in a specific building environment. CFAST is a two-zone fire model used to calculate the evolving distribution of smoke, fire gases and temperature throughout compartments of a building during a fire. These can range from very small containment vessels, on the order of 1 m3 to large spaces on the order of 1000 m3. </p>

<p>Note: You can subscribe to the SVN Commit Log at http://groups.google.com/group/cfast-svn, and Issue Tracker Changes at http://groups.google.com/group/cfast-issues these groups are Announcement Only and allow users to watch Issue Tracker and Subversion activity through email.  </p>

<p>DisclaimerCFAST and Smokeview software are developed at the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) by employees of the Federal Government in the course of their official duties. Pursuant to Title 17, Section 105 of the United States Code. This software is not subject to copyright protection and is in the public domain. NIST assumes no responsibility whatsoever for use by other parties of its source code, documentation or compiled executables, and makes no guarantees, expressed or implied, about its quality, reliability, or any other characteristic.  </p>

<p>These World Wide Web pages in general and the CFAST and Smokeview software in particular are provided as a public service by the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST). With the exception of material marked as copyrighted, information presented on these pages is considered public domain and may be distributed or copied. Use of appropriate byline/photo/image credits is requested.  </p>

<p>The US Department of Commerce makes no warranty, expressed or implied, to users of the Consolidated Fire and Smoke Transport Model (CFAST), and accepts no responsibility for its use. Users of CFAST assume sole responsibility under Federal law for determining the appropriateness of its use in any particular application; for any conclusions drawn from the results of its use; and for any actions taken or not taken as a result of analysis performed using these tools.  </p>

<p>CFAST is intended for use only by those competent in the field of fire safety, and is intended only to supplement the informed judgment of the qualified user. The software package is a computer model that may or may not have predictive capability when applied to a specific set of factual circumstances. Lack of accurate predictions by the model could lead to erroneous conclusions with regard to fire safety. All results should be evaluated by an informed user.  </p>

<p>Any mention of computer hardware or commercial software does not constitute endorsement by NIST, nor does it indicate that the products are necessarily those best suited for the intended purpose.</p>
 title : The cfjexcel Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>cfjexcelDoes some easy import and export of excel docs using ColdFusion and JexcelApi</p>
 summary : <p>Log4j Abstract API for ColdFusion.</p>

<p>Log4j Introduction:
<br/>Log4j is an open source Java project that gives the developer the ability to control which log statements are output with arbitrary granularity. It is fully configurable at runtime using external configuration files and most important, it can be utilized within ColdFusion</p>

<p>Project Description:</p>

<p>Coldfusion include log4j internally which is used whenever  tag is employed. However the specified log files can only be saved in a folder which is sometime not accessible (especially in shared hosting). This CFC will enable logging to an arbitary log file without the above mentioned limitation. It also provide additional benefit of setting the max size of the log file created, along with configuration of backup files, the level of logging to output (debug, info, warn, error, fatal), and formatting of the messages.</p>

<p>I would like to thank the Author(s) mentioned in the links as without these I am not sure if I could have written this utility.</p>

<p>Comments and feedback are always welcome. Happy logging</p>

<p>リンクTODO はじめにChaosDAVはWindows上で動作するWebDAVクライアントです。 </p>

<p>WebサーバにIIS, Apache+mod_davを使用している場合、 WebDAVの設定を行うとファイルをアップロードできます。 ChaosDAVはFTPサーバに対するFTPクライアントのように、 WebDAVに対応したサーバにアクセスしファイルの参照・更新を 行います。 </p>

<p>WebサーバへのアクセスにはHTTPプロトコル(TCPポート:80番）を 使用します。 </p>

<p>動作環境Windows XP Windows Vista ※Windowx XPの場合は.net Framework 2.0が必要 </p>

<p>・動作確認サーバ </p>

<p>IIS 6.0(Windows Server 2003) Apache 2.2(Windows Server 2003) </p>

<p>開発について・言語：C# (.net Framework 2.0) </p>

<p>・開発環境 </p>

<p>Windows XP, Vista Visual Studio 2005 Standard(SP1) Visual C# 2005 Express(SP1) </p>

<p>・最新のソースコード </p>

<p>http://code.google.com/p/chaosdav/source/browse/#svn/trunk/ChaosDAV </p>

 title : The chesstools Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>A library of tools for writing chess AI&#39;s, as well as servers, clients, and any other software that requires a chess engine. Speaks proper FEN, SAN, and long algebraic notation. Supports standard chess and chess960 (Fischer-random). Handles move validation and checkmate/ stalemate/ repetition/ 50-move-rule checking. Features server-side timekeeping with optional latency compensation. </p>

<p>The compact minimax AI framework utilizes alpha-beta pruning and transposition tables under the hood. This enables the developer to produce a modern custom bot by simply overriding AI.evaluate. Additionally, chesstools.book provides an intuitive interface for building opening book databases for use in conjunction with an ai. </p>

<p>AI developers are encouraged to install psyco, which will significantly speed up bot performance. </p>

<p>For sample code, see MICS and MICC. Tutorials here.</p>

 title : The chronicle-recorder Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Chronicle records every memory and register write in the execution of a Linux process, using Valgrind to instrument execution at the machine code and system call level. These events are indexed and compressed; from the resulting database the Chronicle query tool can efficiently reconstruct the state of memory and/or registers at any point during the execution. Additional queries such as &quot;when was the last write to location X before time T&quot; and &quot;when was location X executed between times T1 and T2&quot; are also supported. This infrastructure has a variety of possible uses, but the most obvious use is as the basis for powerful debuggers. </p>

<p>Chronicle by itself is not all that useful to anyone except tool builders. If you&#39;re looking for a useful debugger, try Chronomancer, an Eclipse-based UI for debugging C and C++ programs using Chronicle. </p>

<p>Chronicle is released with the permission of Novell. Thanks Novell!</p>

 title : The chronomancer Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The Chronicle framework provides complete register and memory-level recording of Linux processes and efficient queries over the recorded traces. Chronomancer builds on Chronicle by providing a UI for inspecting and querying traces --- effectively an extremely powerful debugger. Chronomancer can display program state for any chosen point in time; find the last write to any given memory location; display the execution path taken through a function (no more stepping!); display correct call stacks in the presence of tail calls or stack corruption; and much more! </p>

<p>Chronomancer supports debugging C and C++ programs with DWARF2/3 debug information such as is generated by gcc. It is implemented in Java as an Eclipse plugin and can integrate with the Eclipse CDT. It offers extension points so other plugins can define new commands, views, event queries, and custom data renderers. </p>

<p>Chronomancer is small, about 10K lines of code, quite new, and has many rough edges and missing features. (There are many features that would be easy to add that no other debugger has ever offered.) However, it can already be used to debug interesting problems; it has already been used to successfully analyze a difficult Firefox garbage collection bug. </p>

<p>Chronomancer is released with the permission of the Mozilla Foundation. Thanks MF!</p>
 summary : <p>This is a WoW database for the Mangos project, </p>

 title : The cing Open Source Project on Open Hub
 title : The circular-application-menu Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Circular-Application-Menu (C-A-M) by Cole Anstey </p>

<p>This is a circular-application-menu (C-A-M) prototype mirroring the same structure as the existing application menu for the GNOME desktop.  This was originally just a paper prototype which I did back in March 2007, and decided to code over Christmas 2007-2008. </p>

<p>Other Implementations </p>

<p>http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pie_menu </p>

<p> A YouTube Videos of C-A-M In Use  </p>

<p>http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nXh1Tm24kTE </p>

<p>http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mNyLu6JoUX8 </p>

<p>http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5yvLfUFHuCc </p>

<p>http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kzV44KmLJrA </p>

<p>Updated </p>

<p>18th May 2009 - Fixed an error where .svg icons were not being used by default over any .xpm alternatives (http://code.google.com/p/circular-application-menu/issues/detail?id=15#c9). </p>

<p>14th May 2009 - Fixed an error where programs were launching and ignoring any arguments (http://code.google.com/p/circular-application-menu/issues/detail?id=15#c5). A command such as the following should now hopefully work &#39;nautilus /home/collie/code/circular-application-menu/&#39;. </p>

<p>4th September 2008 - Added an request to display only one menu at a time (http://code.google.com/p/circular-application-menu/issues/detail?id=7).   The shown menu in the hierachy can be changed via the Page-Up/PageDown/Home and End keys.  Thanks to bitseven. </p>

<p>3rd September 2008 - Fixed an error than some people where experiencing during construction (http://code.google.com/p/circular-application-menu/issues/detail?id=6&amp;can=1).   Thanks to everyone who provided a stack trace. </p>

<p>27th August 2008 - Added a reflection effect by default.  This stresses the processor somewhat; but it can be easily turned off (see below).  Also added a highlight around the edge incase it&#39;s displayed over a black background. </p>

<p>25th August 2008 - Made any &#39;overlapped&#39; portions of a menu by a sub menu translucent by 75%.  This helps to stop the previous visual ambiguity with overlapped menus items merging with the current menu items.  Also changed the small triangle which denoted a sub menu into a glyph to make it easier to differentiate between applications and menu types. </p>

<p>24th August 2008 - Added the ability to specify the emblem to use for the &#39;root&#39; menu.  By default it&#39;s the GNOME logo; but it can now be changed to allow for a specific distro logo.  An Ubuntu one has been provided as an example.  See the &#39;Application Options&#39; section on how to specify your own. </p>

<p>23rd August 2008 - Changed the right mouse button click functionality slightly so it now aligns the currently shown menu to the click coordinate.  Also fixed a bug so it warps the mouse to the centre of the screen when the root menu is initially shown. </p>

<p>28th July 2008 - The menu now uses the blur plugin by default; to blur underneath the menus.  This can be turned off with an optional parameter (see below). </p>

<p>25th July 2008 - Fixed an error that sometimes occurred if the angle for a submenu was over 360.0 i.e. 360.6.  This was a bugger to hunt down as it didn&#39;t ever happen for me, though I got reports that assertions were occasionally happening for other people in this scenario. </p>

<p>8th March 2008 - Initial revision. </p>

<p>Requirements </p>

<p>GNOME </p>

<p>A composited environment (i.e compiz, etc.) </p>

<p>gtk+ 2.12 </p>

<p>compiz-devel </p>

<p>Installation </p>

<p>svn checkout http://circular-application-menu.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ circular-application-menu </p>

<p>cd circular-application-menu </p>

<p>make </p>

<p>su -c &quot;install -m755 circular-main-menu /usr/bin&quot; or  sudo install -m755 circular-main-menu /usr/bin </p>

<p>Usage: </p>

<p>circular-main-menu OPTION... - circular-application-menu. </p>

<p>Help Options: </p>

<p>-?, --help               Show help options </p>

<p>Application Options: </p>

<p>-h, --hide-preview 
<br/>Hides the menu preview displayed when the mouse is over a menu. </p>

<p>-w, --warp-mouse-off 
<br/>Stops the mouse from warping to the centre of the screen whenever a menu is shown. 
<br/>-g, --glyph-size=S 
<br/>The size of the glyphs 1=small 2=medium 3=large (default). 
<br/>-b, --blur-off 
<br/>Stops the blur from underneath the menu. 
<br/>-e, --emblem=E 
<br/>Specifies the emblems (colon separated) to use for the root menu ./pixmaps/ubuntu-emblem-normal.png:./pixmaps/ubuntu-emblem-prelight.png. 
<br/>-t, --render-tabbed-only 
<br/>Only shows the currently tabbed menu. 
<br/>Adding as a panel launcher </p>

<p>Right-click on any vacant panel space and choose &#39;Add to Panel&#39; from the displayed context menu.  When the &#39;Add to Panel&#39; dialog opens, enter these details (ignore the quotes). Name: &#39;Circular Applications Menu&#39; Generic name: &#39;Circular Application Menu&#39; Comment: &#39;A Circular Application Menu Representation.&#39; Command: &#39;circular-application-menu&#39; Type: &#39;Application&#39; Icon: &lt; Pick one you like, I haven&#39;t designed one yet! &gt; Run In Terminal: &lt; Choose this option so the command that does not create a window in which to run. &gt; When you click on a menu segment the segment disappears and its displayed as the tab of the child menu.  You can also use Page-Up, Page-Down, Home and End keys to navigate. </p>

<p>Making C-A-M the default menu for Alt+F1 (Metacity) </p>

<p>Change the existing &#39;Main Menu&#39; to Alt+F3: </p>

<p>gconftool-2 --set --type string /apps/metacity/global_keybindings/panel_main_menu &quot;F3&quot; 
<br/>Assign C-A-M as being Alt+F1 </p>

<p>gconftool-2 --set --type string /apps/metacity/keybinding_commands/command_1 circular-main-menu 
<br/>gconftool-2 --set --type string /apps/metacity/global_keybindings/run_command_1 &quot;F1&quot; 
<br/>Anything Else </p>

<p>Page-Up/PageDown - Quick jump between menus in the hierachy. 
<br/>Home/End - Jumps to the root menu or last sub menu.

 title : The ciui-dev Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This is a development code base for CiUI. All bug fixes, features and patches will first be checked in here before releasing it as a version to clientside&#39;s repository. </p>

<p>CiUI is an alternate solution to iUI. It is built on the same principles as iUI with a few key differences: </p>

<p>AJAX calls are performed after a page slides DOM doesn&#39;t get overloaded with &quot;pages&quot; as they load. Instead, two DIVs are constantly being reused Page titles are set on the source page, not on the destination page Only specified &quot;a&quot; tags are assumed a part of the UI Some of the features of CiUI include: </p>

<p>Support for forms in two different ways (in-page update or submit to other page) On-demand page caching (via classname annotations)  Pagination (loading more content within one page) </p>

<p>Here are some items on the to-do list: </p>

<p>Create a handle to a custom content processing function. Instead of simply grabbing content of my_page.htm, users will the option to process and display the page content as they wish. Utilize CSS3 transforms and animations to perform hardware-accelerated animations </p>

<p>You can read more information on the announcement blog post here: http://www.clientcide.com/cnet-js-standards/ciui-cnet-iphone-ui </p>

<p>and here: http://ajaxian.com/archives/ciui-cnet-iphone-ui </p>

<p>Also join our group here: http://groups.google.com/group/ciui </p>

<p>Current version is 0.3. Download it here </p>

<p>Release notes </p>

<p>version 0.3 </p>

<p>New feature: page caching.  When you annotate your link with classname cache, i.e. My Page the page will be cached. Meaning, navigating to that page again will not fire a new Ajax request. </p>

<p>Bug Fixes: The cancel function now functions properly (ciUI.cancel()) when you&#39;re trying to cancel a loading page When a new page is requested while the current one is still loading, the current page will stop loading before trying to load the new one. (This was causing unexpected content appear after users navigated away from a page). Fixed an issue with the back button where it would sometimes be disabled when trying to get to the very first page in the hierarchy.  Checkboxes return correct values in Firefox  version 0.2 </p>

<p>New feature: pagination. Load More will load content from loadmorecontent.php and append it to the existing content. This will allow you to do dynamic pagination within page context.  New feature: form processing. Thanks to Aaron Newton for this! There are two ways you can submit a form: . This will submit the form and populate my_element with the output of processform.php.  . This will submit the form, slide to a new page and output results of processform.php to it.  You can find a demo of all features here.  </p>

<p>version 0.1 </p>

<p>initial release</p>

 title : The cl-gambol Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Gambol provides basic propositional unification and search capabilities for Common Lisp.  The code is a modification of an older library from the CMU AI repository, Frolic. </p>

<p>I have removed from Frolic some code specific to the Cray, as well as references to the &quot;Frobs&quot; system which gives Frolic its name.  See AlterationsFromFrolic for all the changes I&#39;ve made. </p>

<p>A small taste: </p>

<p>GAMBOL&gt; (*- (mortal ?x) (human ?x))
<br/>((MORTAL ?X) (HUMAN ?X))
<br/>GAMBOL&gt; (*- (human ?x) (man ?x))
<br/>((HUMAN ?X) (MAN ?X))
<br/>GAMBOL&gt; (*- (human ?x) (woman ?x))
<br/>((HUMAN ?X) (WOMAN ?X))
<br/>GAMBOL&gt; (*- (woman gertrude.stein))
<br/>((WOMAN GERTRUDE.STEIN))
<br/>GAMBOL&gt; (*- (man socrates))
<br/>((MAN SOCRATES))
<br/>GAMBOL&gt; (do-solve-all (?who) &#39;((mortal ?who))
<br/>          (format t &quot;~A is mortal~%&quot; ?who))
<br/>SOCRATES is mortal
<br/>GERTRUDE.STEIN is mortal
<br/>NIL
<br/>GAMBOL&gt; You can drop out to Lisp functions, LOP for operators you care about the results for, LISP for side effects with no truth value to worry about. </p>

<p>GAMBOL&gt; (*- (length nil 0))
<br/>((LENGTH NIL 0))
<br/>GAMBOL&gt; (*- (length (?? . ?t) ?n)
<br/>            (length ?t ?n1)
<br/>            (is ?n (lop (1+ ?n1))))
<br/>((LENGTH (?? . ?T) ?N) (LENGTH ?T ?N1) (IS ?N (LOP (1+ ?N1))))
<br/>GAMBOL&gt; (??- (length (a b c 1 2 3) ?l))</p>

<p>?L = 6
<br/>NO
<br/>GAMBOL&gt; See the API documentation for further details, and Examples for a few common Prolog examples in Gambol. </p>

<p>Third release (0.93) on December 5, 2009.  Changes from 0.02: </p>

<p>removed code designed to coddle an implementation of lisp almost no one uses (and isn&#39;t even Common Lisp, to boot) more minor style adjustments made it possible to work with multiple rulebases </p>

<p>Second release (0.02) on July 10, 2008.  Changes from 0.01: </p>

<p>some irritations with symbol packages in the operators dealt with (i.e., you don&#39;t have to state the package on is) added pl-asserta to add rules to the head of the database made pl-assert and pl-asserta available to the Gambol language with Prologesque names asserta and assertz. added pl-retract to the Lisp API and retract to Gambol (fail) is now a hard-coded part of Gambol, so you can&#39;t accidentally declare it to be true</p>

 title : The cl-jpegmeta Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>CL-JPEGMETA is a library for image metadata manipulation. It currently reads and writes IIM-style IPTC fields, but will hopefully support EXIF fields and XMP metadata at some point in the future. </p>

<p>DependenciesThis relies heavily on the binary data parsing routines introduced by Peter Siebel in his excellent book. Without them, I don&#39;t think I&#39;d even have bothered writing this. </p>

<p>The code is self-contained, though, and doesn&#39;t have any external dependencies. </p>

<p>Current versionThe current version is 0.0.1. I don&#39;t know if version numbering is meaningful this early, though. </p>

<p>Tested onI&#39;ve run CL-JPEGMETA on SBCL (1.0.?, under Windows XP and Mac OS X (intel)), LispWorks Personal Edition (Windows XP) and CLISP (Windows XP). </p>

<p>Example usagecl-user&gt; (require &#39;jpegmeta)
<br/>NIL
<br/>cl-user&gt; (defparameter my-jpeg (jpegmeta:read-jpeg-from-file &quot;foo.jpg&quot;))
<br/>JPEG
<br/>cl-user&gt; (jpegmeta:get-iptc-fields jpeg)
<br/>((:OBJECT-NAME . &quot;Example image&quot;) (:BYLINE . &quot;Fredrik Appelberg&quot;) 
<br/> (:CAPTION-ABSTRACT &quot;This is just an example image with rather pointless metadata.&quot;))
<br/>cl-user&gt; (defparameter my-modified-jpeg 
<br/>           (jpegmeta:set-iptc-fields my-jpeg 
<br/>              &#39;((:OBJECT-NAME . &quot;Modified image&quot;)
<br/>                (:CAPTION-ABSTRACT . &quot;New metadata that overwrites the previous stuff.&quot;))))
<br/>MY-MODIFIED-JPEG
<br/>cl-user&gt; (jpegmeta:write-jpeg-to-file my-modified-jpeg &quot;modified-foo.jpg&quot;)ContactKindly direct bug reports, praise, flames, etc. to fredrik.appelberg@gmail.com</p>

 title : The cl-period Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This library is partly inspired by Perl&#39;s Time::Period library, but now owes more to the time classes of cfengine.  There was a Ruby Quiz (#114) to do something similar, but they called it a time &quot;window.&quot;  It&#39;s intended for use in long-running — or frequently running — programs whose action may be limited to particular time frames.  For example, if a program is empowered to send me a page I might want to tell it only to do so during work hours. </p>

 title : The cl-rogue Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>eeks to create a collection of macros for extracting and generating relationships between information using ontologies for the Semantic Web, which will leverage DSpace, use Protege as the relationship mapper for OWL generation and be tested using MIT’s Piggy Bank extraction project. This is research using Lisp to develop macros for generating and processing semantic data, similar to RacerMaster, particularly the processing of OWL &amp; RDF vocabularies and establishing relationships faster using functional programming to rapidly generate ontological relationships.  </p>

<p>It is also hoped that this project will apply speed paths based off of research from Eugene Agichtein &amp; Silviu Cucerzan regarding predicting performance of relational extraction tasks (RE). This project seeks to re-create some of the work done by with RacerPro, however the focus of this project will be on developing a language model for Reasoning Systems primarily to allow for an open-source and vibrant community of developers to continue the work of improving reasoning systems to drive the Semantic Web. </p>

<p>The exact idea for this project is presented in a paper: “Building Ontological Data From Lists For Semantic Processing”, which is being readied for Conference on Information and Knowledge Management (CIKM 2006). It relies heavily on s-xml, cl-prevelance and cells. </p>

<p>The project has the following goals: </p>

<p>develop easy to use macros for T-Boxes, A-Boxes, ect. process OWL Lite / OWL DL documents. implement SHIQ. implement the OWL-QL query processing system from RasterPro for compatibility. Plug in to modelers such as Stanford’s Protege.</p>

 title : The cl-strings Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>cl-stringsThe package cl-strings contains string functions modeled on Java&#39;s String class for use in SBCL Common Lisp programs.  It depends on Edi Weitz&#39;s regular expression library, cl-ppcre.  The package is designed to be a convenience library familiar to non-lisp programmers. </p>

<p>Although I don&#39;t think this library offers a lot of additional functionality or convenience on top of what Common Lisp already offers, I think it&#39;s useful as a tool for learning how to put together a CL library, and a way to explore the idea that we might come up with libraries similar to other languages as a bridge to new developers. </p>

 summary : <p>Clarion Open Source @ Google CodeEvery tool has its following. Clarion is a useful and interesting tool in that it can nearly completely insulate its users from the sometimes ugly details of the Windows API. Living within the confines of its generated code can make one exceedingly productive, albeit at the expense of flexibility. </p>

<p>Clarion&#39;s third-party market has always been lively, and has (IMO) made a crucial contribution to the longevity of the product. Add-ons are a welcome  necessity (regardless of your choice of core tool) that ease the process of dealing with large or complex subsystems often needed in product development. Don&#39;t want to become a TCP/IP expert? Catalyst Development&#39;s SocketTools, or CapeSoft&#39;s NetTalk make the dirty work easy. In my mind a socket expert is an excellent mechanic, so I have both tools. </p>

<p>You just can&#39;t buy every gadget you need. </p>

<p>Code Is PoetryTo be truly flexible, one has to write a bit of code now and then. Imagine that! If you&#39;re going to write it, it&#39;s good to share as much as you can. And that&#39;s why this open source project exists. </p>

<p>What is Clarion?Shamelessly Ripped from Soft Velocity&#39;s Web Site Clarion is a software development tool to help you get your business applications  
<br/> completed up to 10 times faster. Clarion features a Template driven Code Generator that 
<br/> automates the creation of complete Database Applications. Clarion features roundtrip Code 
<br/> Generation, which means that it preserves all of your hand-written code while still 
<br/> allowing you to make changes and re-generate your application, or any part of your 
<br/> application, as often as needed. Clarion can help you create higher-quality, more 
<br/> consistent database applications in less time.</p>

 title : The clbiff Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>A python script that lists email in the configured boxes. Supports only Maildir mail boxes.  </p>

<p>Ideal for use in the shell prompt, or screen hardstatus line Usage:  </p>

<p>clbiff -1 </p>

<p>Flags: </p>

<p>-1 : Displays a one line (no newline character) summary of mailboxes. </p>

<p>Configuration: </p>

<p>Edit the clbiff file and change the line defining &quot;boxes&quot; near the start of the file. The format is </p>

<p>path to maildir, name, short name), ... </p>

<p>Screen shots: </p>

<p>http://code.google.com/p/clbiff/wiki/Screenshots</p>
